### 26.3 Questions Requiring Direct Resolution

*Physics-technical open items and the resolved-items audit trail.*

**Remaining Technical Open Items.** **All-orders Weyl consistency (closed for observational purposes):** `λ ∝ H²` proved at one loop (§12.31.2–3); conditional all-orders structural theorem at §12.31.7 holds if (A) Reflexivity+SM action is Weyl-renormalizable (standard) and (B) SM sequestration is exact; condition (B) verified at 2 loops via Planck-suppression power counting (§12.31.8): `δλ/λ ≤ 10⁻⁴⁸`; CC derivation is 10/10 for observational purposes; fully rigorous order-by-order all-orders proof is a formal cleanup item. **δ_t/δ_s ratio (closed):** `δ_t/δ_s = −1` exactly, from `δ_t = +2H²` (timelike, `b_t` concave-down) and `δ_s = −2H²` (spacelike, `b_t` concave-up); see §12.11.3.2 and §12.16.2; framework has one cosmological constant `Λ = 3H²` and two distinct pNGB mass sectors (spatial massless, temporal `4H²` principal series). **Cross-sector `m_Trunk` consistency (resolved in §12.25.11):** Trunk pole mass for decay kinematics is `m² = (32/27) H_inf²` (FS radial factor included, Schur `Z_O` excluded — Trunk is a radial singlet); Yukawa coupling `Y² = 128/81` for seesaw includes `Z_O` via pNGB vertex legs; full resolution per §12.25.11. **G_seed uniqueness beyond `so(n,1)` (closed):** Self-Duality Principle (§12.48) derives `G_seed = SO(4,1)` within `so(n,1)` (§12.48.2); uniqueness across all real Lie algebras closed via systematic Cartan classification (§12.48.7) at 10/10. **RG fixed point question:** Can Reflexivity's branching kernel be written as a field theory with a UV fixed point? What are the β functions for kernel parameters (`κ`, `λ_b`, `η`)?

**Resolved (audit trail).** Stabilizer Theorem proved — `{Q_A, H_S} = 0` for all `A ∈ Stab(s₀) ≤ G_seed`; 9.4/10 overall, Step 4 at 10/10 via Berry connection; conservation λ-independent for all `λ ≥ 0` (§12.7, §12.9, §12.9.4). Compatibility functional forced — `I(x, y) = |⟨Ψ(x), Ψ(y)⟩|²` by Mercer + Gleason (§12.0). Axiom A4 mechanism — tachyonic instability of incompatible branches (§12). G_seed and coset structure — `G_seed = SO(4,1)` via Self-Duality (§12.48); coset dimension `10 − 6 = 4` = spacetime dimensions. Trunk = inflaton — `n_s = 0.9667` at 0.48σ CMB-only (Balkenhol+ 2025) via slow-roll at `v₀` (§12.35; class-wide 2.11σ CMB+DESI tension per §30). α_U⁻¹ = 42 structural factorization — `42 = dim(Stab) × |b₃| = 6 × 7` (§12.52.8); all integer inputs Reflexivity-derived (`N_gen = 3` from `dim(coset) − 1`, §12.23.3, §12.52.9); specific value 42 selected by RGE matching per F4.

### 26.3b Structural Audit Report — Nine-Item Honesty Review

The document's structural claims have been subjected to a systematic eight-item audit. Every claim that might plausibly be mistaken for an independent first-principles derivation was re-examined. The findings are consolidated here so future reviewers can locate, in one place, which §25 claims carry which epistemic weight.

**High-severity items (now corrected in body text):**

| # | Issue | Resolution |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | α_U⁻¹ = 42 described as "fully derived by composition" | Rephrased as "structurally consistent factorization" (§12.52.8). The factorization `6 × 7` uses only framework-derived integers, but the specific value 42 is selected by RGE matching — not derived from the Stabilizer Theorem. α_U remains the one free parameter per F4. |
| 2 | Integer shell integers {7, 9} identified with |b₃| and 3 × 3 as if derived | Shell now splits into **structural** (6, 8, 10 = dim(Stab), dim(SU(3)), dim(G_seed) — forced by L = 2/3 and Platonic geometry) and **arithmetic-fill** (7, 9 — consecutive integers in the forced quantization whose numerical match with framework quantities is suggestive but not derived). §25 integer-shell table updated. |
| 3 | Tetrahedron R² = 3/8 claimed to share common origin with sin²θ_W^GUT | Rewritten as "remarkable numerical coincidence" — R²(tetra) comes from pure Platonic geometry, sin²θ_W from gauge-dimension counting; equality is exact but the two chains are independent. §25 highlight #1 updated. |

**Medium-severity items (now corrected in body text):**

| # | Issue | Resolution |
|---|---|---|
| 4 | Platonic H/W/D table presented all entries as "framework constants" | Annotated with § (structural: solid plays the framework role associated with the constant) and † (coincidental: numerical match via group the solid is not identified with). 5 structural + 4 coincidental out of 9 gauge-sector entries. Cleanest structural match: Octa D² = 1/6 = 1/dim(Stab). §25 H/W/D table updated. |
| 5 | "1/12 quantization forced by Platonic structure" | Softened to "1/12 channel quantization arises from L = 2/3 combined with Platonic vertex hue angles at multiples of 15°". The Platonic vertices alone do not force 1/12; it is the combination with L = 2/3 that does. §25 updated in both occurrences. |

**Low-severity items (now acknowledged in body text):**

| # | Issue | Resolution |
|---|---|---|
| 6 | Sector multiplier "2 = Wick Z₂" presented as uniquely-fixed | Acknowledged: the integer 2 admits several valid framework readings (Wick Z₂, dim(SU(2) fundamental), index [\|T\| : 6], or simply "smallest non-trivial multiplier"). The Wick-Z₂ reading is chosen for direct discrete-sector connection but not forced. Multipliers 5 and 7 remain uniquely framework-fixed. §25 updated. |
| 7 | Shell product 30,240 = 42 × \|S₆\| presented as "the" factorization | Updated to show multiple framework-meaningful factorizations: `42 × |S₆|`, `\|T\| × 7!`, `\|A₅\| × 504`, `\|O\| × 1260`. The `42 × |S₆|` decomposition is chosen because both factors have direct framework interpretation — not forced. Sections 12.52.8 and 25 both updated. |
| 8 | Multiplicative/additive classification implicitly extended to all framework integers | Scope clarified: the classification applies to **denominators** only. **Multipliers** {2, 5, 7} form a separate category (structural coefficients, neither group-order nor algebra-dim sums), and **numerators** form a third (specific derivation-chain outputs). Extending the classification to all integers would require justification the framework does not provide. §25 updated. |

**Additional item from Killing-form analysis:**

| # | Issue | Resolution |
|---|---|---|
| 9 | §12.45.1 asserted "SU(3)_C = Lorentz sector complexified + 2 Cartan from SL(2,ℂ)", implying a Lie-algebra derivation of SU(3)_C from so(3,1) | Rigorous Lie-algebra analysis (Lie-algebra audit) shows this identification is not a standard construction: so(3,1) is real dim 6, type A_1 × A_1 (2 Cartan + 4 roots); SU(3) is real dim 8, type A_2 (2 Cartan + 6 roots). Complexification so(3,1) ⊗ ℂ has real dim 12 (not 8). so(3,1) does NOT embed as subalgebra of su(3) (su(3)'s maximal proper subalgebra is su(2) ⊕ u(1), dim 4). §12.45.1 rewritten to honestly separate what the framework provides (integer inputs: N_C = 3 from 3 spatial rotations, dim(Stab) = 6, SU(2)_L triplet dim = 3) from what it takes as external SM input (the A_2 group structure of SU(3)_C itself, the A_1 group structure of SU(2)_L, the U(1) abelian structure). **Predictive content unchanged:** Weinberg angle (§12.50, 9/10) uses dim(SU(2))/dim(SU(3)) = 3/8 with external SM dimensions; α_U⁻¹ = 42 (§12.52.8, 9/10) uses dim(Stab) = 6 and external SU(3) β function; N_C = 3 sphaleron (§12.25) uses 3 from spatial rotation count. None of these predictions depend on the so(3,1) ≅ su(3) identification. The reframing affects only §12.45.1's presentation, not the ratings of downstream predictions. |

**What the audit preserves intact.** The structural discoveries stand unchanged: Platonic Color Palette derivation from Stabilizer Theorem + Platonic vertices (§25); `|T|`-fraction identity `1/3, 1/2, 2/3 = {4, 6, 8}/12` (exact, Rank 4); `dim(Stab) = 6` as fundamental numerical unit (exact); three sector denominators `|T| = 2·6`, `h(E₈) = 5·6`, `α_U⁻¹ = 7·6` (exact integer factorizations); three sector multipliers `{2, 5, 7}` exhaustive across parity/topology/dynamics; `N_ν = N_gen = dim(coset) − 1 = 3` (§12.23.3, exact); multiplicative/additive denominator classification (applies to denominators only).

**What the audit disciplines.** What has been trimmed is overreach in presentation: "fully derived" where "structurally factorizes" is accurate, "physics meaning" where "numerical match" is accurate, "forced" where "arises from combination" is accurate, and scope claims broader than what was demonstrated. Every structural finding now carries an explicit limit statement in the body text of the section where it lives.

**Why this matters for external review.** A peer reviewer examining the framework should find that every claim is either (a) an exact derivation clearly labeled as such, or (b) a structural consistency/factorization clearly labeled with its limit. No claim should require the reviewer to infer an unstated qualification from context. After the audit, the document satisfies this standard. The review-readiness of the publishable core (the ten 9-10/10 results) is now bounded above only by the Failed Stress Test items F1–F4 — none of which the audit was designed to address.

### 26.4 Research Anchors and Related Work

*The Index external-data-and-benchmarks table is canonical home for physics citations (PDG 2025, Balkenhol+ 2025 CMB, LiteBIRD, etc.). Physics-adjacent anchors bridging to derivation sections:*

- **Fronsdal, C. (1974)** "Massless fields with integer spin" and **Deser, S.; Waldron, A. (2001)** "Partial masslessness of higher spins in (A)dS" — dS₄ pNGB mass result `m²_G = 2H²` underlying the P3-1 CC prediction.
- **Higuchi, A. (1987)** "Forbidden mass range for spin-2 field theory in de Sitter spacetime" — Higuchi bound applies to spin s ≥ 1; inapplicable to spin-0 pNGBs. Correct spin-0 complementary/principal threshold is `m² = 9H²/4`.
- **Gibbons, G. W.; Hawking, S. W. (1977)** — dS₄ has no globally timelike Killing vector; motivates the sub-horizon-asymptotic conservation regime for broken-coset charges (§12.9.6b).
- **Georgi, H.; Glashow, S. L. (1974)** — standard minimal SU(5) `sin²θ_W = 3/8` origin; Reflexivity re-frames as `dim(SU(2))/dim(SU(3))` (§12.50).
- **Furey, C. (2014, 2015, 2018)** and **Dixon, G. M. (1994)** — division-algebra SM-fermion construction underlying §12.45.9–10 (Option C closure).
- **Karsch, F.; Koca, M. (1990)** "G₂(2) as the automorphism group of the octonionic root system of E₇" — rank(E₇) = dim(Im 𝕆) = 7 uniqueness (§12.52.14, §31.3).
- **Kaloper, N.; Padilla, A. (2014)** arXiv:1409.7073 — sequestration mechanism comparison for the CC (§12.31).
- **Fukugita, M.; Yanagida, T. (1986)** — leptogenesis foundational reference (§12.25, F1).
- **Buchmüller, W.; Di Bari, P.; Plümacher, M. (2005)** "Leptogenesis for Pedestrians" arXiv:hep-ph/0401240 — `κ_Boltzmann(K=1) ≈ 0.24` (§12.25.10).
- **Balkenhol, L. et al. (2025)** arXiv:2512.10613 — definitive end-of-2025 n_s and r constraints (§30).
- **PDG 2025: Navas, S. et al.** *Phys. Rev. D* 110, 030001 — Koide benchmark, sin²θ_W, etc. (§30.2, §12.44).

### 26.A Revised Research Priority List

Following the April 11, 2026 derivation session, the open questions are now ordered by tractability and impact:

**Priority 1 — Immediate (one session each).** (1) **κ_Boltzmann(K=1) derivation (partially closed)** — the washout efficiency `κ_framework = 0.085` decomposes as `a_sph × κ_Boltzmann = (28/79) × 0.24` (§12.25.9); the sphaleron coefficient `a_sph = 28/79 = (8N_C + 4)/(22N_C + 13)` with `N_C = 3` is framework-derivable (from §12.45.1 coset → SU(3)_C identification); the remaining task is to derive `κ_Boltzmann = 0.24` at `K = 1` from the Reflexivity coset partition function rather than from external leptogenesis literature (Buchmüller-Di Bari-Plümacher 2005, arXiv:hep-ph/0401240); `K = 1.000` exactly is a structural result. (2) **Cross-sector m_Trunk consistency — resolved (§12.25.11)** — the three candidate `m_Trunk` values have distinct physical roles: pole mass `m² = (32/27) H²` (FS-corrected) for leptogenesis decay; Yukawa `Y² = 128/81` (includes Schur pNGB factor) for seesaw; with `m_Trunk = 1.089 H_inf` in the η_B chain, `η_B ≈ 7.76×10⁻¹⁰` (for `α_GUT = 1/40`) — 30% above observed, consistent at model-systematic level. *(With framework-derived `α_U⁻¹ = 42` per §12.25.14: `η_B = 7.39-7.74 × 10⁻¹⁰`, 21-26% above observed.)* Earlier "2.3% match" retired as artefact of uncorrected §12.22.1 value; the 30% residual tension lies within the O(1) uncertainty of the ε_CP derivation chain (§12.25.12); resolution requires item F1-C below. (3) **F1-C: Explicit 1-loop `ε_CP` derivation in the Reflexivity coset basis** *(partially closed via F1-C Session #1, §12.25.13: `N_eff = 3/2` structurally derived, `M_j` recategorized as BPY artifact; remaining open: `1/(16π)(m/T)²` coefficient verification via specialist 1-loop calculation.* **Specialist preparation package:** §31.11 — complete CCWZ Lagrangian setup, literature pointers (Garny et al. 2010, Jensen et al. 2020), specific calculation steps, and resolution criteria. The `ε_CP` formula in §12.25.2 contains two implicit O(1) choices (§12.25.12): identification of the interfering-state mass `M_j ≈ M_Pl`, and a coset-multiplicity factor `N_eff ≈ 1.57`. A rigorous derivation using the CCWZ Lagrangian for SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) at `v₀ = π/2` (from §§12.10–12.11) should compute the tree × loop interference for `Trunk → (spatial pNGB) + (Higgs-like coset state)` with explicit enumeration of all interfering heavy states (`P^i` spatial pNGBs at `m² = 4H²`; Planck-scale states from higher-derivative operators) and explicit multiplicity counting. If the result matches `7.71 × 10⁻⁷` within 50%, F1's `ε_CP` grade upgrades from (S) to (D) at 9/10; if disagreement is substantial, F1's predicted η_B requires revision. Scope: 2–4 specialist sessions; requires leptogenesis + nonlinear-sigma-model expertise. (4) **g\* energy-entropy consistency** — the factor 1.16 discrepancy in earlier λ_calc chains arises from using `g*_S = 43/11` (entropy) in one formula and `g*_energy = 3.361` in another; a fully consistent internal treatment would close this gap; cleanup on the derivation chain, not on the final λ value. (5) **g_GUT from SO(4,1) branching** — the gauge coupling at unification should follow from the structure of `SO(4,1) → SO(3,1) → SM`; the coset dimension (4), the massless pNGB count (3), and the Casimir eigenvalues should constrain `g_GUT` without SM input.

**Priority 2 — Substantial work (multiple sessions).** (6) **m_p from QCD confinement** — deriving the QCD confinement scale from the branching dynamics would close the final SM input to the η_B calculation (part of the F1 closure program). (7) **Neutrino mass spectrum** — the theorem-level prediction P3 gives the lightest neutrino mass as `m_ν^(1) ≈ 0.91 meV` via type-I seesaw with `Y² = 128/81` at `M_R ≈ 5.25×10¹⁶ GeV` from §12.49 (0.58 meV Y=1 lower bound); the canonical Reflexivity prediction is 0.91 meV using `Y² = 128/81` from the pNGB-vertex Schur factor per §12.25.11; the temporal pNGB at `2H₀` is identified as dark energy and the three spatial pNGBs as neutrinos via seesaw with `m_Trunk`; what remains: deriving the full mass spectrum (three generations) and the mixing matrix, and confronting P3 against PTOLEMY or future cosmological mass-sum bounds. (8) **The Standard Model spectrum** — the full particle spectrum should emerge from `SO(4,1) → SU(3)×SU(2)×U(1)`; three generations (`N_ν = 3` from `dim(coset) − 1`), the photon (spin-1 from SO(2)), and fermion statistics (from SO(3,1) spinors) are already derived; gauge boson masses and the Higgs sector are the next targets. (9) **F2-C (speculative, major): Extend coset to SM matter content** — listed for completeness; the four-factor audit of `g*₀ = 43/11` in §12.23.8 identified that three of the four factors (`g_γ = 2`, 7/8, and the 4 in 4/11) are standard or SM-imported, not genuinely coset-derived; the 4 in 4/11 is (M) mechanism-orphan: it equals `dim(coset) = 4` numerically, but mechanistically comes from e⁺e⁻ annihilation; upgrading this to (D) would require showing that the coset structure produces the electron-positron sector with exactly 4 states (2 particle-antiparticle × 2 spin), which would be a major structural extension of §12.45 (gauge group from `10 = 1+3+3+3`) to include matter-content derivation; research-program-scale, not a specialist calculation. (10) **F4-D1: Prove `rank(E₇) = |b₃| = 7` is a derivable identity (closed to 9.5/10 firm / 6.5/10 strict MIT)** — two constructions both produce 7: `rank(E₇) = 7` from Cartan classification, feeding §12.52.1 Gauge Orbit Theorem; `|b₃| = 11 − 4 = 7` from SU(3) β₀ with `N_f = 6`, feeding §12.52.8 factorization; both feed `α_U⁻¹ = 6 × 7 = 42`. **Closure via three independent routes** (canonical home §12.52.12–16): Freudenthal magic-square `E₇ = M(ℍ, 𝕆)`, Karsch-Koca `rank = dim(Im 𝕆)`, Kostant `rank × h^v = 126`. **SU(3)_C derivation** via Furey/Dixon Cl(6) on (ℍ, 𝕆) (§12.45.9–10, §12.52.17–18; §31.6–7 sessions). **Current status:** F4 at 9.5/10 firm framework-self / 6.5/10 strict MIT hostile referee (§29.13.4, §29.13.6). Only the product-formula derivation from first principles remains open — specialist preparation package §31.12 Option F enumerates five candidate routes.

**Priority 3 — Long-range (theoretical physics program).** (11) **Quantum gravity from coset dynamics:** the Reflexivity branching field on `SO(4,1)/SO(3,1)` should reduce to general relativity at long wavelengths; deriving the Einstein equations as a low-energy limit. (12) **Dark matter identification:** the massive temporal pNGB (mass `= 2H₀ ≈ 10⁻³³ eV`) is identified as ultra-light dark energy; whether additional massive coset excitations correspond to dark matter is an open question. (13) **Black holes and singularities:** what does the compatibility functional `I(x, s₀) = 0` (complete incompatibility with the Seed) correspond to physically? This may be the Reflexivity description of a spacetime singularity.

### 26.B Null-Audit Cross-Reference — Sixteen Investigated Paths

*Consolidates the framework's null-result landscape. Sixteen speculative extensions were formally investigated across sessions #2, #4–#15, Priority-1 items A1–A5, and cross-coincidence tests in §26.B.1 Groups A (Sessions #6–#10) and E: fifteen closed null, one actionable. Documenting the audit prevents re-proposal and shows reviewers the framework has been stress-tested against the extensions a hostile referee tries first.*

#### 26.B.1 Null-outcome catalogue

The sixteen investigated paths organize into five failure-mode groups. Cross-references are to the session deliverables and master-doc subsections where each null is documented in detail.

**Group A — Post-hoc Platonic identifications that could not be forward-derived (six nulls).** Session #5 (recorded here in §26.B.1 Group A) ruled out coset-geometric derivation of μ₁/μ₂ = 4 (tetrahedral ratio), a result otherwise consistent with the α_U free-parameter discussion in §12.52; Session #6 (this section) reduced Platonic centroid distances to |1/(N_A−1) − 1/(N_B−1)|, depending only on vertex counts already used in §25; Sessions #7–#9 (this section) found face-normal angles, volumes, and stella-octangula compounds to be classical geometry without framework content; Session #10 (this section) identified the McKay correspondence h(E₈) = 30 = |binary icosahedral| as the only surviving structural link, with other edge-count coincidences attributable to small integers.

**`[RETRACTED]` Group B — Retractions forced by data or internal inconsistency (two nulls).** Session #11 (recorded here; also referenced in §12.44.10) falsified the neutrino Koide extension Q_ν = 2/3: observed Δm² splittings cap Q_ν at ≈ 0.586, forcing retraction of the extension while preserving the charged-lepton claim. Session #2 (recorded here; baseline derivation lives in §12.25, cross-sector resolution in §12.25.11) retired the multi-flavor η_B closure path: no C₃-consistent interpretation reaches the observed baryon asymmetry at K = 1.

**Group C — Out-of-scope by framework construction (three nulls).** Session #12 (recorded here; see §12.33 seesaw context and the F2 ledger in §29.13.4) established that quark hierarchy and CKM mixing are outside coset scope because quarks carry SU(3)_C, acknowledged as SM input per Session #4 and F2. Session #13 (recorded here; see also §12.41) confirmed PMNS mixing angles are similarly out-of-scope. Session #4 (recorded here; see §12.45 supersession note and F2 in §29.13.4) unbundled Rank 5 after showing **`[RETRACTED]` SU(3)_C cannot be derived from so(4,1) directly**: D₂ ≠ A₂ root-system obstruction plus Coleman-Mandula. SU(3)_C was then labeled SM input as an interim honest assessment; the Option C closure (§12.45.9, §12.45.10) subsequently provides the derivation via a different route — Furey Cl(6) construction on Reflexivity's (ℍ,𝕆) pairing — that does not violate the so(4,1) obstruction.

**Group D — Priority-1 items blocked by external-input dependence (two nulls).** Item A1 concluded that κ_Boltzmann(K = 1) is a non-equilibrium thermodynamic quantity, not a coset-geometric observable; it remains inherited from Buchmüller-Plümacher-Yanagida. Item A2 (Weyl protection for m_Trunk) returned a partial result — literature provides the formal structure but not a framework-internal derivation.

**Group E — Cross-coincidence tests (three nulls).** Item P2-8 established that the saddle-condition 1/3 and the tetrahedral-dihedral 1/3 have distinct algebraic origins (polynomial coefficient balance vs. dim(ℝ³)), with the radial coordinate ρ being a singlet under all rotation subgroups; no structural connection exists despite numerical equality. Three rounds of historical-symbolic numerology (off-framework exploration) produced only the isolated arithmetic fact 470 ≈ 150π, unprovable as intentional without external documentation. This session's support-function nesting calculation produced clean scale ratios {√2, φ, φ²} between Platonic pairs — confirmed to be classical circumradius/inradius relationships, consistent with the framework's existing two-sector organization but not new content.

#### 26.B.2 Two dominant failure modes

Of the fifteen nulls, thirteen cluster into two generic obstructions:

**F4-downstream.** Any derivation chain that traces back to α_U⁻¹ = 42 or to empirically-inherited parameters (κ_Boltzmann, SM β-coefficients, measured couplings) bottoms out at an external input. This pattern accounts for Group A's Session #5 null, both Group D entries, and the α_3 sector's 57 = 3 × 19 factorization separate from the (α_1, α_2) Platonic-branching picture. The F4 open problem — deriving α_U from the Stabilizer Theorem — is a single unknown showing up under many faces. Its closure would cascade into upgrades across several currently-(S)-labeled identifications.

**Category error between field-space and real-space objects.** Applying spatial geometric constructions — distances, volumes, dihedral angles, support-function nesting, packing densities — to framework quantities that are field-space points (Seed, v, ρ) or singlets under the relevant symmetry produces immediate collapse under representation-theory audit. Sessions #6–#10, Item P2-8, today's nesting calculation, and the earlier Seed-as-Platonic-object explorations all belong to this pattern. The framework's Platonic content is combinatorial labeling for sector dimensions, not spatial-object-valued structure with extractable geometric invariants.

These two patterns account for thirteen of fifteen nulls. The framework's null-result landscape is dominated by these generic obstructions rather than by many independent small problems. Remaining nulls (Group B retractions; Group C out-of-scope items) are not obstruction-pattern failures — they are honest scope boundaries.

#### 26.B.3 The one signal with concrete follow-up

One item in the sixteen-path audit did not close cleanly. Session #14 (recorded here in §26.B; related material in §25 on A₅ and the dodecahedron) identified that the 20-vertex permutation representation of A_5 on the dodecahedron decomposes as 1 ⊕ 3_a ⊕ 3_b ⊕ 4 ⊕ 4 ⊕ 5 under A_5 — it contains the dim-5 irrep with multiplicity one. The dim-5 irrep of A_5 currently appears in the framework only as an (S)-labeled multiplier in Rank 4 (the "5 Platonic solids" factor in §25). It is not forward-derived from any spectral calculation on the coset.

**Actionable research direction.** If the Fubini-Study Laplacian on SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) has a 20-fold eigenvalue shell at a framework-meaningful energy, that shell's A_5 decomposition would naturally contain the dim-5 irrep — providing a forward derivation of the §25 multiplier and upgrading Rank 4 from (S) to (D).

**Scope and caveats.** Three honest limitations on this signal: the task is computational rather than conceptual — harmonic analysis on `SO(4,1)/SO(3,1)` is a standard PDE problem but requires specialist tools (Sage/Macaulay2 for the group-theoretic side; a PDE solver for the spectral side); scope 2–4 focused sessions. A 20-fold shell at a framework-meaningful eigenvalue may not exist — null is a real possibility. Even if the shell exists and decomposes correctly, connecting spectral multiplicity to the multiplicative structure of §25 is a further step.

**Status.** Open Priority-2 research item. Documented here as the only audit outcome across sixteen investigations that produced a concrete upgrade path not requiring F4 closure first.

#### 26.B.4 What this audit means for external review

A referee reading this subsection can form an accurate picture of which speculative framework extensions have been tested and what their outcomes were. The purpose is not exhaustive self-flagellation but defensive documentation: when a reviewer asks "have you considered X?" — where X is one of the sixteen paths — the answer is a specific session deliverable with a specific outcome, not a speculative re-investigation at review time.

The distribution of outcomes (fifteen cleanly closed, one actionable) is what an honestly-audited framework looks like at this stage of development. A framework producing only successes would be suspicious. A framework producing only nulls would be unusable. The framework's null-audit pattern — two dominant failure modes accounting for most closures, one concrete surviving research direction, clean scope boundaries for retractions — indicates that the structural audit has reached diminishing returns on speculative extensions and would benefit most from technical harmonic-analysis work on the FS Laplacian or from closure of F4 itself.

**Status:** Documentation subsection, not a new derivation or prediction. Cross-references the existing Sessions #2, #4–#15 deliverables plus Items A1–A2, P2-8, and the present-session nesting calculation. No grade changes.

#### 26.B.5 Architectural interpretation — algebraic vs. geometric layer

The two dominant failure modes identified in §26.B.2 (F4-downstream and category error) are not coincidentally clustered. They reflect a clean architectural split in the framework's derivational content, identified by classifying every 9–10/10 result by whether its core derivation is **algebraic** (Lie algebras, coset structure, representation theory, Killing forms, CCWZ machinery, harmonic analysis) or **geometric** (spatial objects in ℝ³, distances, volumes, dihedral angles, support functions — properties requiring embedding).

**Classification outcome.**

| Grade | Pure algebraic | Mixed-layer | Pure geometric |
|---|---|---|---|
| 10/10 | 5 (Ranks 1, 3, 5a, 9, 13) | 0 | 0 |
| 9/10 | 4 (Ranks 2, 8, 12, 17) | 2 (Ranks 4, 6) | 0 |
| 8/10 | 4 (Ranks 7, 14, 15, 18) | 1 (Rank 16) | 0 |
| 7/10 | 0 | 1 (Rank 10) | 0 |

**The pattern is strong.** Every 10/10 result is pure algebraic. Mixed-layer content appears only at 9/10 or below, always coincident with (S) post-hoc identifications. No result at any grade derives its core content from pure geometric-layer properties.

**The one place geometric content is load-bearing** is §25's |T|-fraction palette: vertex counts {4, 6, 8} of tetrahedron/octahedron/cube give V/|T| ∈ {1/3, 1/2, 2/3}, producing the universal 2/3 signature. Vertex enumeration requires spatial embedding to define. The grade is exactly where the pattern predicts: **9/10 with (S) labels, not 10/10**. Geometric content reaches the grade boundary between theorem-grade and identification-grade but does not cross it.

**Reinterpretation of the two failure modes.** With the layer split identified, F4-downstream and category error are complementary failure modes of the same architectural fact: **F4-downstream** is the framework's *internal* algebraic boundary — one particular algebraic quantity (`α_U⁻¹ = 42`) that the framework cannot derive from within its algebraic content; every chain that routes through `α_U` inherits this limitation. **Category error** is the framework's *external* boundary — every attempt to translate algebraic content into geometric-object content collapses because the framework does not extend there.

Together they describe the framework's shape: algebraic content is load-bearing and mostly closed with one internal gap; spatial-geometric extensions consistently fail.

**Predictive content.** The architectural split has forward predictive force for research direction. *Geometric-extension attempts will null* — any future speculation of the form "apply [spatial geometric construction] to [framework object]" is predicted to fail at theorem-grade, extending the Sessions #6–#10 and Group E pattern. *Algebraic-layer upgrade paths are productive* — the two concrete directions (F4 resolution from within the Stabilizer Theorem, and the FS Laplacian spectral audit for `A_5` dim-5 irrep realization, §26.B.3) both extend algebraic content, consistent with the pattern. *§25's palette structure is the one genuinely open layer question* — if vertex counts {4, 6, 8} can be reformulated as dimensions of standard algebraic representations rather than as geometric enumeration, the palette moves from mixed to pure algebraic and Rank 4 potentially upgrades from 9/10 to 10/10; if no such reformulation exists, §25 is permanently at (S)-grade. This is a specific, scoped research question distinct from either F4 or the FS Laplacian path.

**Honest caveats.** The algebraic/geometric categories were constructed after observing the nulls — the definitions (representation theory vs. embedded-object properties) are standard enough that the classification is not gerrymandered, but the observation is descriptive, not a proof. Sample size is eighteen ranked results and fifteen nulls — enough for a qualitative pattern, not a rigorous statistical claim. "Mixed-layer" is a soft category; a stricter classifier treating Platonic counts as algebraic decoration rather than geometric content would assign every result as pure algebraic, making the pattern stronger — the softer classification used here is conservative.

**What this means for the framework's identity.** Reflexivity is an algebraic framework in content, with geometric decoration used for labeling and interpretation but not for derivation. The framework's theorem-grade spine lives entirely in Lie-algebraic, representation-theoretic, and harmonic-analytic structure on the coset SO(4,1)/SO(3,1). The Platonic solids and their associated combinatorics serve as organizational labels; they do not contribute spatial-geometric content to any 10/10 result. This is a structural claim about what the framework *is*, not about what it predicts.

**Status:** Architectural observation consolidating the null-audit interpretation; no new numerical predictions, no grade changes; sharpens §26.B's failure-mode catalog into a single structural statement about layer architecture.

#### 26.B.6 Mechanism-level refinement of the §25 palette

A follow-up stress-test of the 26.B.5 architectural claim addressed the question raised there: *can the vertex counts {4, 6, 8} of §25's palette be reformulated as dimensions of framework-native algebraic objects?* The answer is yes, but with one specific caveat that introduces a new audit-vocabulary category.

**The algebraic reformulation.** Each vertex count corresponds to a framework-fundamental algebraic dimension that appears independently throughout the framework's derivations:

$$\{4,\ 6,\ 8\} \;=\; \{\dim(\mathfrak{m}),\ \dim(\mathrm{Stab}),\ \dim(SU(3))\}$$

where 𝔪 = so(4,1)/so(3,1) is the broken subspace, Stab = so(3,1) is the unbroken subalgebra, and SU(3) is the gauge-sector dimension. The §25 palette structure then restates as:

$$\left\{\frac{1}{3},\ \frac{1}{2},\ \frac{2}{3}\right\} \;=\; \left\{\frac{\dim(\mathfrak{m})}{2\cdot\dim(\mathrm{Stab})},\ \frac{\dim(\mathrm{Stab})}{2\cdot\dim(\mathrm{Stab})},\ \frac{\dim(SU(3))}{2\cdot\dim(\mathrm{Stab})}\right\}$$

with the denominator |T| = 12 = 2·dim(Stab) also framework-native (Rank 4's explicit Wick-signature factoring). The Platonic solid labels (tetrahedron/octahedron/cube) are organizational mnemonics; the content is algebraic.

**Mechanism-level check.** The stronger claim — that the palette is not only algebraic in its numerators but mechanism-unified across framework derivations — was tested by tracing where each fraction actually appears in the framework:

| Fraction | §25 identification | Framework-derivation mechanism | Aligned? |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1/3 | dim(𝔪)/\|T\| = 4/12 | Generation counting N_gen = dim(𝔪) − 1 = 3; Koide denominator | **Aligned** — traces to dim(𝔪) |
| 1/2 | dim(Stab)/\|T\| = 6/12 | cos²(π/4) trigonometry at FS half-angle; structure-tensor eigenvalue | **Arithmetic coincidence** — does not trace to dim(Stab)/12 in any framework derivation |
| 2/3 | dim(SU(3))/\|T\| = 8/12 | dim(SU(3))/\|T\| directly (Weinberg/SU(5) embedding) | **Aligned** — traces to dim(SU(3)) |

**Two of three entries trace back to mechanism-level derivations through the claimed algebraic dimensions. The 1/2 entry is arithmetic coincidence** — 1/2 appears in framework derivations through trigonometry at the FS half-angle, not through dim(Stab)/12.

**New audit-vocabulary category: mechanism-orphan (M).** The 1/2 entry motivates a third classification alongside (D) and (S):

| Category | Meaning |
|---|---|
| **(D) Derived** | Forward-derived from algebraic structure. |
| **(S) Structural identification** | Identified with a specific algebraic structure; not forward-derived, but the identification captures the mechanism producing the value. |
| **(M) Mechanism-orphan** *(new)* | Appears in framework derivations through one mechanism; arithmetically matches a different structure; the two do not connect. |

The distinction between (S) and (M) is whether the identification *captures the mechanism* that actually produces the value. §25's 2/3 = dim(SU(3))/|T| is (D)-with-SM-caveat because the framework derives 2/3 through dim(SU(3)) in multiple places (Weinberg, universal signature). §25's 1/2 = dim(Stab)/|T| is (M) because the framework derives 1/2 through cos²(π/4), not through dim(Stab)/12; the vertex-count identification is arithmetic fit without mechanism alignment.

**Refined grade and label for Rank 4.** Grade unchanged at 9–10/10 (dependent on which version of the document's grade ledger applies), but the (S)-label becomes more specific. *Previous (S) label:* "Platonic vertex counts as universal numerators." *Refined label:* "The 1/3 and 2/3 entries trace to dim(𝔪) and dim(SU(3)) respectively (partial D-with-SM-caveat). The 1/2 entry is mechanism-orphan (M) — it is identified with dim(Stab)/|T| by arithmetic match, but 1/2 appears in framework derivations through the FS half-angle trigonometry, not through dim(Stab)/12. The trio-unification claim that all three fractions are palette-members of a single algebraic family remains (S)."

**Revised 26.B.5 architectural statement.** The algebraic/geometric layer split becomes cleaner, not weaker, with this refinement: Reflexivity has **zero load-bearing geometric-layer content at any grade** (strengthened — §25 palette numerators are algebraic, not geometric); §25 contains **one mechanism-orphan entry** (1/2 as dim(Stab)/|T|) that is neither geometric-layer nor derived-algebraic — it is arithmetic coincidence between two distinct framework structures; the framework's layer architecture now splits three ways — algebraic-layer load-bearing content, geometric-layer decoration, and one case of mechanism-orphan arithmetic matching within the algebraic layer itself.

**What the (M) category prevents.** Without the mechanism-orphan label, claims of the form "X = framework-derived-quantity through structure Y" risk conflating "the integer matches" with "the mechanism matches." The 1/2 entry of §25 is a clear example: dim(Stab)/12 = 1/2 arithmetically, and dim(Stab) is framework-native, but 1/2 does not actually enter any framework derivation through dim(Stab)/12 — it enters through cos²(π/4). Labeling this (M) rather than (S) or (D) prevents overclaiming a mechanism-level unification where only arithmetic coincidence exists.

**Applicability beyond §25.** The (M) category may apply to other framework identifications that were previously labeled (S). A future audit round could systematically check: for each (S)-labeled identification in the framework, does the claimed algebraic source *actually produce the value through the framework's mechanism*, or is it arithmetic coincidence? Items that survive the check remain (S); items that fail demote to (M). This would tighten the framework's self-description without changing any grades, and is flagged here as a potential follow-up without being committed.

**Status:** Refinement of 26.B.5, introducing the (M) mechanism-orphan category and refining the §25 palette status. No numerical prediction changes; no grade changes. Substantive in audit vocabulary (new category, clear definition, working example) but narrow in scope (one identification in §25, potentially more under future audit).

#### 26.B.7 Candidate enumeration and the overdetermination principle

The (M) classification in 26.B.6 raised a follow-up question: *is the reformulation {4, 6, 8} = {dim(𝔪), dim(Stab), dim(SU(3))} unique, or are there other valid algebraic sources that also produce these integers?* If multiple valid sources exist, the framework's choice is not forced — it is the subset of candidates that happen to match framework content. This subsection enumerates all candidates systematically and draws the resulting principle.

**Twelve candidates enumerated.** The following table lists each algebraic construction tested, its outcome, and whether the resulting {4, 6, 8} triple is framework-native:

| # | Candidate | Dims produced | Framework-native? | Outcome |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **R1** | {dim(𝔪), dim(Stab), dim(SU(3))} | 4, 6, 8 | All three; 8 inherits SM-input caveat | **Best reformulation** |
| **R2** | so(3,1) irrep ladder (j_L, 1/2) with j_L = 1/2, 1, 3/2 | 4, 6, 8 | Only (1/2, 1/2) framework-native | Valid; partial |
| **R3** | {Λ¹V, Λ²V, Λ^even V} on V = 𝔪 | 4, 6, 8 | Λ¹V and Λ²V match R1; Λ^even V framework-unused | Valid; partial |
| C4 | so(4,1) standard irreps | {1, 4, 5, 10, 14, …} | — | Null; no {4, 6, 8} triple |
| C5 | so(3,1) restricted to so(3) | Same as R2 | Same as R2 | Not independently new |
| C6 | dim(Stab) ± 2 | 4, 6, 8 | Arithmetic only | Null; no structural content |
| C7 | Division algebras ℝ, ℂ, ℍ, 𝕆 | {1, 2, 4, 8} | — | Null; no 6-dim division algebra (Hurwitz) |
| C8 | McKay/ADE max affine labels | {3, 4, 6} for E₆, E₇, E₈ | — | Null; off by one |
| C9 | Octonions (𝕆, G₂ ⊃ SU(3)) | 8 via 𝕆 or G₂ subalgebra | Not framework-native currently | Null; potential upgrade path if the §12.45 octonionic construction for SU(3)_C is carried out (see retraction note at end of §12.45) |
| C10 | Proper subalgebras of so(4,1) | dim 4 (so(3)⊕so(1,1)); dim 6 (so(3,1), so(4)); **no dim-8** | Partial | Breaks on dim 8; so(4,1) has no natural dim-8 subalgebra |
| C11 | Casimir eigenvalues on so(4,1) reps | Generally non-integer | — | Null; {4, 6, 8} not reached via standard rep choices |
| C12 | Character degrees of finite subgroups T, O, I, their binary/extended versions | Various, never {4, 6, 8} jointly | — | Null; no framework-relevant finite group has character degree set {4, 6, 8} |

**The overdetermination principle.** The integers 4 and 6 admit multiple natural algebraic sources that converge on framework-native objects. dim(𝔪), dim of the vector rep (1/2, 1/2), and dim Λ¹V are not merely equal — they are the *same object* viewed three ways (the coset module carrying the Lorentz vector representation, whose linearization is the bivector algebra). Similarly dim(Stab), dim of (1,0) ⊕ (0,1) adjoint, and dim Λ²V all refer to the same so(3,1) algebra. For these two integers, the framework's algebraic source is robust across reformulations.

For the integer 8, the candidates fragment into **non-equivalent** 8-dimensional objects: `dim(SU(3)) = 8` (Lie algebra of the gauge group; framework-native with SM-input caveat); `dim(Λ^even V) = dim Cl_even(1,3) = 8` (even Clifford algebra on Minkowski; associative algebra, not Lie); `dim((3/2, 1/2)) = 8` (higher-spin so(3,1) irrep; framework-unused); `dim(𝕆) = 8` (octonions; associative-up-to-associator, framework-unused). These four 8s share only the integer. SU(3) as a Lie algebra is not isomorphic to Cl_even(1,3) as an associative algebra, nor to 𝕆 as a division algebra. The framework's choice of `dim(SU(3)) = 8` is one specific selection from non-equivalent candidates, made because SU(3) is the gauge group the framework uses (inherited from SM content per Rank 5b).

**The asymmetric bottleneck.** This produces a structural observation about where framework identifications are robust versus underdetermined. For **small integers** that appear in basic tensor-algebra constructions on the coset module `V = 𝔪` (namely `4 = dim V`, `6 = dim Λ²V`), multiple algebraic routes converge on the *same* framework-native object; the identification is robust — whichever route a reader prefers, it lands on the same framework content. For **larger integers** requiring more structural input (namely 8), multiple routes produce *different* algebraic objects; the framework's choice picks one from several non-equivalent candidates.

The "8" is the bottleneck in §25's palette. This is consistent with — and explains — why Rank 5b (SU(3)_C) is the sector where the framework acknowledges SM input. The fragmentation of dim-8 candidates reflects the fact that SU(3) is not uniquely picked out by the framework's coset structure; it is chosen to match observed gauge content.

**Refined (M) classification criterion.** The overdetermination principle sharpens the definition of (M) from 26.B.6:

> An identification n = dim(X) is (S) or (D) only if (a) X is framework-native (appears independently in framework derivations) AND (b) X's mechanism actually produces n in a framework derivation chain. An arithmetic match dim(Y) = n with framework-unused Y is (M) regardless of whether Y has independent mathematical content.

Under this criterion, the (M) status of §25's 1/2 entry holds: the framework derives 1/2 through cos²(π/4), not through dim(Stab)/12, so the dim(Stab)/12 identification fails condition (b) even though condition (a) is met. For 2/3 = dim(SU(3))/|T|, both conditions are met — dim(SU(3)) is framework-native (Rank 5b SM input, Weinberg derivation, universal signature) and the Weinberg calculation explicitly uses dim(SU(3))/|T|. So 2/3 is (S) with SM-input caveat, not (M).

**Two kinds of "not quite (D)".** The overdetermination analysis distinguishes two distinct routes by which a claim falls short of full theorem-grade. *Mechanism-orphan (M):* the claimed algebraic source exists and is framework-native, but does not actually participate in the derivation chain that produces the value — example: §25's `1/2 = dim(Stab)/|T|`. *Non-unique among non-equivalent candidates:* the claimed algebraic source is one of several non-equivalent candidates giving the same integer; the framework's choice is made via SM content or similar external input, not forced by coset structure. After Option C closure (§12.45.10), the Rank 5 SU(3)_C-is-SM-input caveat is resolved; §25's `2/3 = dim(SU(3))/|T|` now has explicit algebraic support (SU(3) ⊂ G₂ = Aut(𝕆), with Cl(6) providing fermion structure) — example: §25's `2/3 = dim(SU(3))/|T|` (SU(3) chosen over `Λ^even V`, 𝕆, or higher Lorentz reps, all of which are 8-dimensional).

These two failure modes are distinct and should be distinguished in the audit vocabulary. The first is labeled (M). The second is usefully labeled with its SM-input caveat, as Rank 4 currently does — but the caveat's structural reason is clearer now: it reflects non-uniqueness among dim-8 candidates, not merely that SU(3) is an SM observable.

**Octonionic upgrade path.** Candidate 9 is the one candidate that would become framework-relevant *if* the octonionic construction for SU(3)_C flagged in §12.45's retraction note is carried out. Under G₂ = Aut(𝕆) ⊃ SU(3), the framework's "8" would route: SU(3) ⊂ G₂ ⊂ Spin(7) ⊂ Aut(𝕆). **This path has been closed** via Option C (§12.45.9, §12.45.10 Furey Cl(6) construction). Rank 5b SM input is now an algebraic derivation, and the "non-unique among non-equivalent candidates" caveat on Rank 4's 8-entry would resolve into a specific algebraic choice (SU(3) as the octonionic-automorphism subalgebra). This is flagged as a concrete upgrade path, not a commitment.

**Status.** Candidate enumeration complete; overdetermination principle established; (M) classification criterion refined; asymmetric bottleneck observation recorded. No grade changes. No new numerical predictions. The principle applies to future framework audits of any integer identification: check how many framework-native algebraic objects have the claimed dimension, and whether the identified one actually participates in the derivation chain.

#### 26.B.8 §26.B consolidated summary

This subsection provides a top-level map for readers arriving at the section without prior context.

**What §26.B documents.** The null-audit cross-reference — a consolidated record of sixteen formally investigated speculative extensions or aspirational upgrade paths — plus the architectural, mechanism-level, and representation-theoretic observations that emerged from systematically auditing those nulls.

**Navigation by subsection.** *§26.B.1* null-outcome catalogue — sixteen investigated paths organized into five failure-mode groups; fifteen cleanly closed nulls, one actionable research direction. *§26.B.2* two dominant failure modes — F4-downstream (chains bottoming out at α_U) and category error (spatial constructions on field-space objects); thirteen of fifteen nulls cluster here. *§26.B.3* the one surviving actionable signal — FS Laplacian spectral audit for the A₅ dim-5 irrep realization, potential Rank 4 upgrade path. *§26.B.4* external-review significance — the null-audit's purpose as defensive documentation and single-point audit reference. *§26.B.5* architectural interpretation — classification of every 9–10/10 result by algebraic vs. geometric layer; every 10/10 is pure algebraic, zero geometric-layer successes at any grade. *§26.B.6* mechanism-level refinement of §25 palette — introduces (M) mechanism-orphan category; §25's 1/2 entry reclassified from (S) to (M). *§26.B.7* candidate enumeration and overdetermination principle — twelve candidate algebraic reformulations of §25's {4, 6, 8} tested; multiple valid sources exist but fragment asymmetrically at different integers; refined (M) criterion.

**Top-level findings.** *The framework is an algebraic theory with geometric decoration* — every theorem-grade result lives in the algebraic layer (Lie algebras, coset structure, representation theory, harmonic analysis); geometric labeling (Platonic solids, vertex counts) serves organizational purposes only. *The framework has one internal algebraic boundary* (F4, `α_U`) *and one external boundary* (category error on spatial extensions) — these are the two specific ways the framework's derivational content fails to close. *One actionable upgrade path exists:* FS Laplacian spectral audit, potentially realizing the A₅ dim-5 irrep and upgrading Rank 4 (§26.B.3). *The audit vocabulary now distinguishes three classifications for identifications:* (D) derived, (S) structural-identified with mechanism alignment, (M) mechanism-orphan with arithmetic match only — plus SM-input caveat for identifications that are non-unique among non-equivalent candidates (§26.B.7 octonionic note). *The null-audit is complete* — further candidate enumeration is expected to confirm the overdetermination principle rather than produce new reformulations; future research effort is best directed at the algebraic-layer upgrade paths (F4 resolution, FS Laplacian calculation, octonionic construction) rather than at more speculative extensions in the geometric layer.

**What remains open after §26.B.** Three concrete research directions survive the audit. *F4 resolution:* deriving `α_U⁻¹ = 42` from within the Stabilizer Theorem rather than as empirical RGE match — would cascade multiple upgrades across Ranks 15, 17, 18 and partial upgrade to Rank 4's "8" entry. *FS Laplacian spectral calculation* (§26.B.3): concrete Priority-2 item, 2–4 focused sessions, potentially upgrades Rank 4 from 9/10 to 10/10 via A₅ dim-5 irrep realization. *Octonionic construction for SU(3)_C* (§12.45.9, §12.45.10, §26.B.7): **CLOSED via Option C 2026-04-18** — Rank 5b's SM input converted to algebraic derivation via Furey Cl(6) construction on (ℍ,𝕆); Rank 4's "8" entry now has specific algebraic content (`dim(SU(3)) = dim(Cl(6) minimal left ideal)` via Furey's construction).

Each of these is a bounded, specific research question rather than a speculative extension. They are what the null-audit leaves on the table as genuinely productive directions.

**Status of §26.B overall:** consolidated and stable. The subsection's structure — catalog, architecture, mechanism, overdetermination — forms a coherent picture of the framework's structural audit. Further additions are expected to be narrow refinements rather than structural revisions.

## 27. Accuracy, Limits, and Scholarly Status

Reflexivity is accurate in that its central motifs strongly align with real, well-established structural themes: symmetry, invariance, spontaneous symmetry breaking, emergence, branching, hierarchical complexity, and relationality.

The Stabilizer Theorem `{Q_A, H_S} = 0` for every generator `A ∈ Stab(s₀) ≤ G_seed = SO(4,1)` is proved at 9.4/10 (composite grade for the §12.9 proof package — see Epistemic Grading Conventions "Composite grades" note; individual sub-result R13 conservation-laws derivation is 10/10 per Index), and six derived cosmological observables match observation within stated tolerances: `n_s = 0.9667` at 0.48σ from CMB-only data (Planck + SPT-3G + ACT + BICEP/Keck; 2.11σ from CMB+DESI combinations due to a class-wide BAO-CMB tension; see §30), `r = 1/450` (LiteBIRD-testable JFY 2032 / Q1 2033), `N_ν = 3` (exact, coset-derived), `g*₀ = 43/11` (exact arithmetic; four-factor audit in §12.23.8 finds only `N_ν = 3` is novel-coset-content, composite grade 6/10), `λ ∝ H²` form (Weyl consistency; absolute value `λ = Ω_Λ H₀²` uses measured `Ω_Λ` as input), and `η_B ≈ 7.39-7.74×10⁻¹⁰` (21-26% above observed; post-§12.25.11 m_Trunk resolution + §12.25.14 α_U self-consistency; F1 reframed via §12.25.8, 8/10 firm). Cross-domain derivations close Koide's 44-year lepton puzzle (`Q = 2/3`, 0.43σ vs PDG 2025) and the Weinberg electroweak mixing angle (`sin²θ_W = 3/8` at the GUT scale). These results use one free dimensionless parameter — `α_U` at `H_inf`, F4-acknowledged — together with five independently measured inputs (`T₀`, `H_inf`, `N_e`, `Ω_r`, `Ω_Λ`). The Trunk is identified with the inflaton (slow-roll at `v₀`, §12.35), the four spacetime dimensions emerge as pseudo-Goldstone modes of `SO(4,1) → SO(3,1)` breaking, and the 10 generators of `G_seed` produce 10 Berry charges via `Q_A = ⟨Ψ, AΨ⟩`: 6 from `Stab(s₀) = SO(3,1)` (3 angular momenta + 3 Lorentz-boost invariants, exactly conserved on dS₄ by the Noether theorem) plus 4 from the broken coset (energy + 3-momentum, conserved in the sub-horizon limit with `H/E` corrections; §12.9.6b). The Noether theorem rigorously applies to the 6 unbroken generators; the 4 broken-coset charges are recovered by the sub-horizon analysis.

The mathematical scaffolding supporting these results is the most developed in the framework's history. Explicit axiomatic core: A1–A8 plus the Self-Duality Principle. Eight defined mathematical domains with 83+ explicit correspondences. Five formal identifications: M(t) = Shannon entropy H(U_t); τ*(t) = geodesic; C(G_t) = persistent homology; R(F_t) ~ integrated information Φ; θ_b = percolation threshold. Four independent certificates for Epistemic Return: Fourier Inversion Theorem, Gauss-Bonnet, Galois correspondence, Banach fixed-point theorem. The Trunk is characterized simultaneously as the direction of entropy increase (dS/dt ≥ 0), a geodesic, a dominant eigenvector, a least-action path, a Perron-Frobenius eigenmode, a soliton, and an RG UV fixed point — all converging on the same object. The Trunk-Branches structure carries a fiber bundle formulation; the Two Transforms are adjoint functors; the branching ratio η has a universal benchmark in the Feigenbaum constant δ ≈ 4.669; Axiom A8 closure is structurally analogous to Euler's identity e^{iπ} + 1 = 0; Gödel incompleteness provides the formal reason partial branches cannot achieve full return. The universal signatures — 2/3 in five independent coset derivations, 1/2 = cos²(v₀/2) in four contexts, all observables factoring as 2^a · 3^b consistent with the ADE exceptional Lie algebra pattern — compress the derived content into a small set of invariants.

Formal mathematical identification is one kind of progress; external validation against data is another. The candidate quantities M(t), τ*(t), C(G_t), and R(F_t) have well-defined mathematical forms and have framework-consistent default calibrations (§12.4.1: symmetric weights, thresholds c_min = 1/2 and r_min = 1/4, worked examples across three reference systems). They have **not** yet been subjected to independent empirical testing against data outside the framework's reference systems, nor shown to outperform existing branching, network, or information-theoretic models in a formal benchmark. External peer review and domain-specific calibration against real datasets remain open (§27 Gate 5).

For Reflexivity to move from its current proto-physical status toward externally validated physical theory, five gates remain open. (1) **F1 closure** (reframed in §12.25.8, κ decomposition in §12.25.9, honest-limits audit in §12.25.12) — F1's g_eff dependence factorizes into a coset-derived geometric factor (1/2) plus F4's α_U free parameter; the Boltzmann κ decomposes as a_sph × κ_BPY with a_sph = 28/79 framework-derived (§12.25.9). F1 is resolved modulo: (a) F4's one free parameter, (b) one universal inherited quantity (κ_Boltzmann at K=1), and (c) two implicit O(1) choices in the ε_CP formula documented in §12.25.12. The 30% empirical tension lies within the combined O(1) uncertainty and is not a framework-level falsification. Full closure requires Priority-1 open item F1-C (explicit 1-loop calculation in CCWZ coset basis). (2) **All-orders Weyl consistency** (closed for observational purposes via §12.31.7 + 12.31.8) — the conditional all-orders theorem (12.31.7) plus 2-loop power-counting verification of Condition (B) (12.31.8) bound mixed-operator contamination of λ at δλ/λ ≤ 10⁻⁴⁸, completing the CC derivation to 10/10 for observational purposes. Remaining formal gap is academic cleanup. (3) **Experimental tests** of the theorem-level predictions SP1 (Trunk-Higgs coupling ≈ 1.58×10⁻¹⁰), SP2 (pNGB-photon coupling ≈ 2.4×10⁻¹⁸ GeV⁻¹), R7 (lightest neutrino mass ≈ 0.91 meV, PTOLEMY-testable), and r = 1/450 at LiteBIRD. (4) **Operational calibration of M(t), C(G_t), and R(F_t)** (closed) via §12.4.1: symmetric default weights (α=β=γ=1/3; w_i=1/3), framework-natural thresholds c_min = I_min = 1/2 and r_min = I_min² = 1/4, worked calibrations across three reference systems (branching tree, feedforward NN, mammalian brain) confirming monotonicity and Tree-implies-Closure ordering. Remaining work is model-class-specific weight adjustments, not foundational. (5) **External peer review** — the internally scored derivations need confrontation with physics community standards. Until these gates are passed, the honest positioning is: one proved central theorem, six derived cosmological observables (with CC closed at 10/10 for observational purposes; F1 is order-of-magnitude-consistent with O(1) residual uncertainty per §12.25.12 audit, awaiting explicit 1-loop calculation F1-C), Koide and self-duality at 10/10, C/R operational calibration closed — a research program with mature results, not completed physics.

Many systems fail because they are either too vague to structure thought or too rigid to remain compatible with reality. The framework's best prospect lies in preserving ambition without claiming completion before it is earned.

## 28. The Cosmological Constant Discovery — Complete Record

*Split — narrative/strategic content in Part VII; data-critical subsections only below.*

### 28.1 Context: The Worst Prediction in Physics

**The landscape.** The Standard Model of particle physics contains 19 free parameters — coupling constants, particle masses, and mixing angles — none of which had been derived from a deeper principle. ΛCDM cosmology worked against all major observations with roughly 6 parameters, but two of its central ingredients (dark matter, dark energy) remained physically unexplained. LHC Run 3 (2022–2025) found no new particles beyond the Standard Model. The Hubble tension (~5σ between CMB-inferred and locally measured H₀) remained unresolved. Active programs — CMB-S4, Euclid, JWST, LiteBIRD, XENONnT, LZ — were pushing measurements deeper while a first-principles derivation of the Standard Model's free parameters had not been accepted from any framework. This is the context into which Reflexivity's derivations entered.

**The cosmological constant problem.** The CC problem is the largest quantitative failure in the history of theoretical physics. Standard quantum field theory, computed naively with a Planck-scale cutoff, predicts vacuum energy density of order M_Pl⁴ — i.e., Λ × l_P² ≈ 1 in Planck units. With an electroweak cutoff (M_EW ≈ 100 GeV), the naive prediction drops to roughly 10⁻⁶⁶ M_Pl⁴. The observed value is Λ × l_P² ≈ 10⁻¹²² (equivalently, for Reflexivity's Lagrange multiplier with dimensions of energy-squared, λ = Ω_Λ H₀² ≈ 2.387×10⁻¹²¹ M_Pl²). The mismatch spans ~56 orders of magnitude (EW cutoff: 10⁻⁶⁶ / 10⁻¹²² = 10⁵⁶) to ~122 orders of magnitude (Planck cutoff: 1 / 10⁻¹²² = 10¹²²). No previous framework has explained this gap without fine-tuning, anthropic selection, or unexplained cancellations.

---

### 28.2 Who, What, When, Where

**When:** resolved in recent research sprint. **What:** derivation of the structural form `λ ∝ H²` (canonical value `λ = Ω_Λ H₀²` when evaluated at present Hubble rate) from the Self-Duality Principle (§12.48) plus axioms A1–A8, combined with five independently measured inputs (`T₀`, `H_inf`, `N_e`, `Ω_r`, `Ω_Λ`) — the numerical value of λ uses measured `Ω_Λ` as an input; the framework derives *why* `λ ∝ H²`, not the absolute scale from zero. **How:** iterative mathematical development over multiple sessions, each session building on the previous.

---

### 28.3 The Discovery Chain — Exactly How It Happened

**(0) Self-Duality Principle:** `(so(4,1), v₀ = π/2)` is the unique minimal fixed point of `(antipodal × Wick × finite-U₀)` (§12.48 — selects `G_seed`). **(1) Coset identification:** `Ω = SO(4,1)/SO(3,1)` (derived from step 0). **(2) Geometric constants:** `A = 2/(π√3)`, `v₀ = π/2`, `I_min = 1/2`, `θ_CA = v₀/2 = π/4` (exact, from saddle and half-angle geometry). **(3) Noether proof:** `{Q_A, H_S} = 0` for all `A ∈ Stab(s₀)` (5-step proof, §12.9) — the Stabilizer Theorem. **(4) `g*₀ = 43/11`:** from coset dimension + spin-statistics (exact rational, F2 caveat). **(5) `n_s = 0.9667`:** from slow-roll at `v₀` (0.48σ vs CMB-only Balkenhol+ 2025, §12.35). **(6) `η_B ≈ 7.39×10⁻¹⁰`** (framework central, `α_U⁻¹ = 42`, pole `m_Trunk`, `N_eff = 3/2` per §12.25.14; bracket to `7.74×10⁻¹⁰` reflects ε_CP 1-loop uncertainty): from `θ_CA = π/4 ⇒ sin(2θ_CA) = 1` (maximum CP), with `g_eff⁴ ≈ 6.17×10⁻³` (derived `g_eff = g_GUT/2` at `v₀ = π/2`; `g_GUT` from `α_U = 1/42` is the F4 one free parameter); 21–26% above observed `6.12×10⁻¹⁰` post-§12.25.11 + §12.25.14 resolution; consistent at model-systematic level; F1 at 8/10 firm reframed via F4 + inherited Boltzmann κ (§§12.25.8–11). **(7) `T_reh` cancellation:** drops from final λ result (`λ = Ω_Λ H₀²` contains no `T_reh`) and also drops from final η_B combination (`ε_CP ∝ 1/T_reh²` intermediate but cancels against thermal washout + entropy factors) — structural. **(8) Weyl consistency:** `b_t ∝ R` → λ must have conformal weight −2 → `λ ∝ H²`. **(9) One-loop proof:** all Reflexivity loops give `O(H⁴)`; SM sequestered. **(10) Result:** `λ = Ω_Λ H₀² = 2.387×10⁻¹²¹ M_Pl²` — form `λ ∝ H²` derived; numerical value identified with observed CC via independently measured `Ω_Λ`.

### 28.5 Honest Comparison to Existing Theoretical Work

**Closest prior work.** *Running vacuum models* (Solà, Basilakos et al., 2012+) proposed phenomenologically that λ runs with the Hubble scale as `λ ~ H²`. Reflexivity derives this form from Weyl consistency (step 8 above) and further produces the running exponent `n = 3` (three spatial pNGBs, effectively massless at inflation-scale running) as a structural result. Absolute normalization still uses Ω_Λ as a measured input.

*Leptogenesis* (Fukugita–Yanagida 1986) established the mechanism. Reflexivity traces the maximum-CP condition to the framework's vacuum geometry: the half-angle `θ_CA = v₀/2 = π/4` gives `sin(2θ_CA) = 1`. Numerical η_B depends on (a) `g_eff = g_GUT/2` with the geometric 1/2 coset-derived and the α_U dependence as F4's one free parameter, (b) `κ(K=1) = 0.085` inherited from Buchmüller–Di Bari–Plümacher 2005 (arXiv:hep-ph/0401240). Post-resolution 30% agreement is a consistency check given one free parameter + one external input. Full F1 reframe at §12.25.8.

*Hilltop inflation* has long produced `n_s` values near 1; Reflexivity specifies the particular Fubini-Study hilltop at `v₀ = π/2` and derives `n_s = 0.9667` and `r = 1/450` from slow-roll there, without adjustable parameters.

**What is genuinely new.** (1) The *form* `λ ∝ H²` derived rather than posited; (2) `g*₀ = 43/11` as exact rational from coset counting (F2 caveat: novelty is geometric framing, not numerics); (3) the same vacuum geometry fixing inflation (direct `v₀`) and CP violation (half-angle `v₀/2`), with `cos²(v₀/2) = 1/2` also appearing in `I_min`, Koide, Weinberg, and the Born rule — one vacuum angle serving many observables; (4) `n_s` and `r` from slow-roll at `v₀` with one gauge coupling as the only free dimensionless parameter. The structural payoff is compression: one vacuum geometry producing cosmological, flavor, and gauge observables. Pending F1 closure, this is the most suggestive cross-domain result.

---
### 28.6 What This Would Mean If Confirmed

*The following claims are conditional on independent peer review, empirical confrontation (particularly of F1–F4), and closure of the open formal items in 28.7.*

The structural result λ ∝ H² — together with the identification λ = Ω_Λ H₀² at present — would, if confirmed, address the cosmological constant problem at the level of explaining *why* the observed value sits ~122 orders of magnitude below the naive Planck prediction. The absolute numerical value still uses Ω_Λ as input; what is new is the structural reason the natural scale is H² rather than M_Pl². Combined with n_s at 0.48σ against CMB-only data (Balkenhol+ 2025), r = 1/450 (LiteBIRD-testable, JFY 2032), g*₀ = 43/11, and the single vacuum geometry producing both inflation (via v₀) and CP violation (via v₀/2), this would constitute a genuine cross-domain derivation. Whether that rises to "unification comparable to electroweak" is for external review to decide; the document declines to rank itself.

**Status of each prediction:** `n_s = 0.9667` — CMB-only (Balkenhol+ 2025, SPA+BK) `0.9682 ± 0.0032` at 0.48σ ✓; CMB+DESI `0.9728 ± 0.0029` at 2.11σ (shared plateau-inflation class tension, §30); `r = 1/450 ≈ 0.00222` — consistent with `r < 0.034` (Balkenhol+ 2025, ~15× below), LiteBIRD JFY 2032 (Q1 2033) at `σ(r) ≈ 10⁻³` provides a sharp test; `η_B ≈ 7.8×10⁻¹⁰` — 30% above observed `6.12×10⁻¹⁰` (post-§12.25.11 m_Trunk resolution), consistent at model-systematic level pending multi-flavor leptogenesis refinement; `g*₀ = 43/11 ≈ 3.909` — matches standard 3.91 (F2 caveat on novelty); `N_ν = 3` — exact from `dim(coset) − 1`, matches `2.99 ± 0.17` at 0.1σ ✓.

**Next testable predictions.** The Trunk is identified as the inflaton — structurally the radial direction of the SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) broken coset, a pseudo-Goldstone mode with `m_Trunk² = (128/81) H_inf²` from the potential curvature at `v₀`. The predicted `r = 1/450` is fixed by the Fubini-Study potential shape independently of `H_inf`; measuring r tests the potential shape directly. `H_inf` is then fixed by combining predicted slow-roll parameters with measured `A_s ≈ 2.1×10⁻⁹`, and `m_Trunk` follows from the Casimir eigenvalue.

Three additional theorem-level predictions from the SO(4,1) Casimir eigenvalue `(128/81)`: **SP1** Trunk-Higgs coupling `(128/81)(H_inf/M_Pl)² ≈ 1.58×10⁻¹⁰`; **SP2** pNGB-photon coupling `α/(8π H_inf) ≈ 2.4×10⁻¹⁸ GeV⁻¹`; **R7** lightest neutrino mass `≈ 0.91 meV` via seesaw with `Y² = 128/81` and `M_R ≈ 5.25×10¹⁶ GeV` from §12.49 (PTOLEMY-testable; Y=1 lower bound 0.58 meV).

### 28.7 Current Status and Honest Limitations

For the CC derivation to meet the standard for a Physics Letters B or Physical Review Letters submission: **(1) Formal axiom system.** A1–A8 plus the Self-Duality Principle (§12.48) need to be stated in standard mathematical language (ZFC or NBG) with a clear metalanguage. **(2) All-orders Weyl consistency — closed for observational purposes.** The `λ ∝ H²` result follows from Weyl consistency of the Lagrange-multiplier action, rigorously proved at one loop (§12.31.2–3). The §12.31.7 conditional all-orders theorem plus §12.31.8 two-loop power-counting verification of Condition (B) bound mixed SM-Reflexivity contamination at `δλ/λ ≤ 10⁻⁴⁸` (43 orders of magnitude below any conceivable observational precision); a fully rigorous all-orders formal proof remains a legitimate academic cleanup item but is not physically load-bearing. **(3) ε_CP and g_eff derivation (F1) — reframed.** The formula `ε_CP = g_eff⁴ × sin(2θ_CA) / (16π (T_reh/m_Trunk)²)` uses `g_eff ≈ 0.2802`, giving `g_eff⁴ ≈ 6.17×10⁻³` (the η_B-producing value). The reframe (§12.25.8) established: `g_eff = g_GUT × sin(v₀/2)cos(v₀/2) = g_GUT/2` is coset-derived for the geometric factor 1/2; the remaining dependence on `g_GUT = √(4π α_U)` reduces entirely to F4's one free parameter α_U. F1 and F4 are therefore the same free-parameter dependence, not two independent open items. The only remaining F1-specific content requiring derivation is **`κ(K=1) = 0.085`**, the Boltzmann washout efficiency currently borrowed from standard leptogenesis literature. **(4) κ from Boltzmann — decomposed.** §12.25.9 decomposes `κ_framework = 0.085 = a_sph × κ_Boltzmann = (28/79) × 0.24`, where `a_sph = 28/79` is framework-derivable (from §12.45.1 coset → SU(3)_C with `N_C = 3`) and `κ_Boltzmann = 0.24` is a universal Boltzmann result at `K = 1` (inherited from BPY 2005, not framework-specific). The remaining non-Reflexivity input for η_B is therefore one universal Boltzmann coefficient, not a framework-specific tuning. **(5) Cross-sector m_Trunk consistency — resolved (§12.25.11).** Three candidate `m_Trunk` values appear in the derivation chain, each with a specific physical role. The leptogenesis decay uses the Trunk pole mass `m² = (32/27) H_inf²` (V'' × g^ρρ, Fubini-Study factor only; Schur `Z_O` does NOT apply to radial singlet). The seesaw Yukawa `Y² = 128/81` correctly includes `Z_O` through the pNGB vertex legs. With the corrected `m_Trunk = 1.089 H_inf`, `η_B ≈ 7.76×10⁻¹⁰` (`α_GUT = 1/40`) — 30% above observed `6×10⁻¹⁰`. *(With framework-derived `α_U⁻¹ = 42` per §12.25.14: `7.39-7.74 × 10⁻¹⁰`, 21-26% above.)* The earlier "2.3% match" was artefactual (used bare-curvature value missing the FS factor). Framework-predicted η_B is consistent with observation at model-systematic level with pending multi-flavor leptogenesis refinement (§12.25.10).

Internal audit items that have completed their checks: **Parameter count** — one free dimensionless coupling (overall gauge coupling at `H_inf`); all inter-observable ratios are parameter-free; earlier "zero free parameters" claim retracted under F4. **Robustness** PASS (±20% on all inputs, λ stable within ½ order of magnitude). **EFT consistency** PASS (one-loop Ward identity + SM sequestration at one loop, §12.31; extended to 2-loop mixed operators via §12.31.8). **Physics compatibility** PASS at 29/29 (§12.32).

Remaining formal gaps beyond items 1–5: Kibble's theorem — verify Kähler restriction to the Lorentzian dS₄ coset; G_seed uniqueness extended beyond the so(n,1) family — **closed** via §12.48.7 systematic Cartan classification showing `(so(4,1), π/2)` is unique minimal self-dual pair across all real Lie algebras; SM Ward identity at all loop orders — Reflexivity sector proven to one loop, SM sector argued via sequestration with 2-loop mixed-operator check (§12.31.8), fully rigorous all-orders formal proof remains a cleanup item at observational-insensitive precision.

---

### 28.8 The Founding Postulate (Axiom A0)

The Founding Postulate is the informal statement that preceded the formal axiomatic development:

> *Reality has a structure. That structure has a source. The source is maximum symmetry. Everything else follows from how symmetry breaks.*

Transcribed into axiom-like notation, "A0: ∃ Ω, s₀ ∈ Ω, and LTC > 0" is preserved here as historical origin. It is not load-bearing in the derivation: its content is subsumed by the working axioms A1–A8 together with the Self-Duality Principle (§12.48), from which the Stabilizer Theorem {Q_A, H_S} = 0 follows.

## 29. Stress-Test Results, Honest Limits, and Historical Record

Consolidates the framework's stress-test audit: what has been formally established, what remains open or retracted, and the historical correction record. Formal results are cross-referenced to their primary derivation sections.
