### 29.13.4 Honest Limits — F1–F5 Stress-Test Ledger

A framework without honest limits is not a framework; it is a religion. Five items from the stress test (F1–F5; full ledger in §29.13.4) did not pass and require either external work, explicit retraction, or continued monitoring of open experimental questions. §29 acknowledges them directly rather than burying them.

**F1 — Baryon asymmetry η_B ≈ 7.4–7.7×10⁻¹⁰.** The prediction sits 21–26% above observed 6.12×10⁻¹⁰ after the `m_Trunk` cross-sector resolution (§12.25.11) retired the earlier artefactual "2.3% match" from the uncorrected §12.22.1 bare-curvature derivation, and after the α_U self-consistency propagation (§12.25.14) applied the framework-derived `α_U⁻¹ = 42` throughout the η_B chain. A four-pass structural audit on F1 (§12.25.12) identified that F1's residual openness has three distinct items: *(a) F4 dependence* — the F1 reframe (§12.25.8) established that `g_eff = g_GUT/2` factorizes as a coset-derived 1/2 (from `v₀ = π/2`) times F4's free parameter dependence through `g_GUT = √(4π α_U)`; F1 is not independent of F4. *(b) κ_Boltzmann inheritance* — the washout efficiency `κ_Boltzmann(K=1) ≈ 0.24` is inherited from universal Boltzmann physics (§12.25.10); Session #2 of the null audit (§26.B.1 Group B) retired multi-flavor refinement as a closure path for the 30% central-value tension. *(c) Two implicit O(1) choices in ε_CP* (§12.25.12) — the audit identified that the ε_CP formula's coefficient implicitly fixes (i) the interfering-state mass `M_j ≈ M_Pl` (not explicitly derived) and (ii) a coset-multiplicity factor `N_eff ≈ 1.57` (not explicitly computed from the loop); the combined O(1) uncertainty from these two items exceeds the 30% tension, which should therefore be read as order-of-magnitude consistency rather than parameter-free prediction. F1 is accordingly reframed: F4 dependence + κ_Boltzmann inheritance + two implicit ε_CP O(1) choices.

**F1-C Session #1 update (§12.25.13, 2026-04-18):** Two of three (S) items closed structurally. N_eff = 3/2 derived from N_gen × (1/2) 2-body decay kinematics (using framework-derived N_gen = 3 from §12.33.1). M_j = M_Pl 'implicit' recognized as BPY-comparison artifact — the framework's ε_CP is a thermal formula (T_reh/m_Trunk = 12.62 > 1), not a hierarchical BPY formula, so no independent M_j parameter is needed. Using structural N_eff = 3/2 shifts η_B from 7.76×10⁻¹⁰ to 8.12×10⁻¹⁰ (30% → 35% tension) at legacy α_GUT = 1/40; with α_U⁻¹ = 42 per §12.25.14 these shift to 7.39×10⁻¹⁰ and 7.74×10⁻¹⁰ (23% / 26% tension) — honest cost of derivability. F1 grade: 6.5/10 → **7.5/10 firm**. The one remaining (S) item is the 1/(16π)(m/T)² coefficient itself, requiring rigorous 1-loop self-energy calculation in CCWZ coset Lagrangian (F1-C Session #2, specialist preparation package prepared: §31.11).

**α_U self-consistency closure (§12.25.14):** the legacy η_B chain used `α_GUT = 1/40` as SM-input gauge coupling in §12.22.3, while §12.52 derives the framework's own unification coupling as `α_U⁻¹ = 42`. Propagating the framework-self-consistent value through the η_B chain (see §12.25.14 full propagation table) gives `η_B(phenomenological N_eff = 1.57) = 7.39 × 10⁻¹⁰` (21% above observed, was ~29% at legacy obs 6.0); `η_B(structural N_eff = 3/2) = 7.74 × 10⁻¹⁰` (26% above observed, was ~35% at legacy obs 6.0). This closes the implicit F4-dependence item (a) identified in the four-pass audit: F1 was not independent of F4's α_U treatment, and the previous tension numbers mixed `α_U⁻¹ = 40` (legacy) with `α_U⁻¹ = 42` (derived) across different subsections. The framework now has one consistent α_U value throughout.

**F1 grade: 7.5/10 firm → 8/10 firm.** Justification: (i) two of three (S) items structurally closed (F1-C S#1), (ii) α_U self-consistency closed (§12.25.14), (iii) F4 dependence item (a) closed by α_U self-consistency, (iv) κ_Boltzmann BPY inheritance justified (§12.25.10) with multi-flavor refinement retired (§26.B.1 S#2), (v) m_Trunk labeling audit complete (§12.25.11, §12.42.4, §12.49.2). The remaining open item is the 1-loop CCWZ coefficient (S3), quantitatively important but structurally well-defined — this is the specialist residue targeted by §31.11 F1-C Session #2. Current status: framework-self-consistent prediction with 21–26% tension within documented O(1) uncertainty bracket [4, 10] × 10⁻¹⁰ which contains the observed 6.12 × 10⁻¹⁰. Full 9–10/10 closure requires external 1-loop calculation execution.

**F2 — g*₀ = 43/11.** The number is exact arithmetic and matches observation to ~0.05% (`g*₀ = 43/11 = 3.909`; modern SM value with `N_eff = 3.046` gives 3.911). A four-pass structural audit (§12.23.8) found that the derivation's four ingredients factorize as: `g_γ = 2` (photon polarizations from SO(2) little group of SO(3,1)) — (D) Derived, 10/10, legitimate but standard; `N_ν = 3` (from `dim(coset) − 1 = 3` spatial pNGBs labeling generations per §12.33.1) — (D) Derived, 8/10, genuine framework contribution; **7/8** (Fermi-Dirac weight) — (S/SM-imported) 5/10; earlier §12.23.5 incorrectly claimed "DERIVED from SO(3,1) spinors"; §12.33.1 establishes pNGBs are bosons, so 7/8 applies to SM fermions (`N_R`, `e±`), not coset content; §12.23.5 revised in this audit pass; **4 in (4/11)** ratio — (M) mechanism-orphan, 4/10; coset `dim = 4` numerically matches `2·g_γ_after = 4`, but the mechanisms (broken-generator count vs entropy conservation in e⁺e⁻ annihilation) are different; arithmetic match, not structural.

**Composite honest grade: 6/10 pre-Cl(6); 8/10 firm post-Cl(6) upgrade (§12.23.9).** The pre-Cl(6) audit correctly noted only N_ν = 3 was genuinely coset-derived beyond textbook cosmology. After the Furey/Dixon Cl(6) closure (R5, §12.45.9–10, §31.6–7) derives SM fermion content from the (ℍ, 𝕆) Clifford algebra, the remaining factors become framework-derived: 7/8 from Cl(6) spinor content + spin-statistics theorem, and 4/11 from Cl(6)-derived electron content + e⁺e⁻ annihilation kinematics. The result now stands as "four framework-derivable factors via coset + Cl(6)" rather than "three standard factors × one coset-derived factor." R11 grade conditional on R5's 8.5/10 firm and bounded by it. What earlier required F2-C speculative work is now closed through the R5 Cl(6) channel.

**F3 — "7 as third structural primitive."** Early drafts claimed 7 (from e₇ or from 1+3+3, and in the broader form "four primitives {2, 3, 7, φ}") as a generating number alongside 2 and 3. More careful examination shows 7 never appears as a free prime in Reflexivity observables — the 7 in α_U⁻¹ = 42 = 6 × 7 is |b₃| (SU(3) one-loop beta coefficient = 11 − 4 = 7; §12.52.8), a derived arithmetic consequence of SU(3) Yang-Mills + 3 generations, not a coset-geometric primitive. Similarly, 5 in h(E₈) = 30 = 5 × 6 is an arithmetic consequence, not a primitive; and φ does not appear in α_U at all. The "third/fourth primitive" claim is retracted. The retraction was propagated in this audit pass from §29.13.4 into its actual textual source: §12.51.4 (renamed from "The Primitive Basis {2, 3, 7, φ}" to "Origin of the Integer Factors in α_U = 1/42"), §12.51.6 (new retraction subsection), §25 discovery 3 ("exhaustive" language removed), and front-matter line 371 ({2, 5, 7} "each sourced from a distinct physical sector" softened to observation, not exhaustiveness theorem). The Platonic encoder uses **2 and 3 only** as coset-geometric primitives; 5 and 7 are derived arithmetic quantities.

**F4 — Zero-parameter meta-claim.** The statement "Reflexivity has zero free parameters" is strong and was published in earlier drafts. On careful accounting, Reflexivity has one free dimensionless coupling (the overall gauge coupling at H_inf) and takes three dimensional scales (M_Pl and v_EW directly measured; H_inf inferred from CMB A_s combined with framework-predicted r = 1/450, so H_inf is framework-entangled rather than independently measured — per MIT stress test F4-A audit, §12.43). The "zero-parameter" claim is therefore replaced by the more precise "one free dimensionless parameter; all ratios parameter-free." This is still unusually constrained — the Standard Model has 19 — but the stronger meta-claim failed its own stress test.

**F4 partial closure (R1 + R1.6 × 2 + R1.5 Sessions, 2026-04-18):** The free parameter α_U⁻¹ = 42 has received substantial structural reduction via four research sessions (R1, R1.5, R1.6 #1, R1.6 #2).

*R1 Session #1 result (§12.52.12):* Freudenthal magic-square analysis establishes E₇ = M(ℍ, 𝕆) as the unique exceptional algebra selected by Reflexivity's (ℍ, 𝕆) division-algebra pairing. Given this pairing, **rank(E₇) = 7 is a theorem**, and only (ℍ, 𝕆) among 10 magic-square entries produces 42 under the product formula α_U⁻¹ = rank × dim(Stab).

*R1.6 Session #1 result (§12.52.13):* Attempted first-principles derivation of the product formula. Paths C and D returned null. A second framework-native formula emerged: (dim(E₇) − rank(E₇))/N_gen = 126/3 = 42, with a striking cross-GUT match at E₆ → MSSM α_U⁻¹ = 24.

*R1.6 Session #2 result (§12.52.15):* Exhausted further candidate paths. Paths A (anomaly matching), B (holographic dS/CFT), E (Jordan/FTS), K (56 − 14 E₇-specific), L (Stabilizer counting) all null. Path F (Casimir-ratio h^v(G)/h^v(so(4,1))) unifies Session #1's two candidates via Kostant's dimension formula for simply-laced Lie algebras. The candidate-formula landscape has two distinct candidates, not three. Product formula remains ansatz; specialist input needed for full closure.

*Option B Session #1 result (§12.52.16):* Search for third independent cross-GUT data point. **Negative:** no independent third data point found. **Positive unexpected result:** among all simple Lie algebras, **only E₇ satisfies rank × h^v = 126**, so the Casimir-ratio formula at α_U⁻¹ = 42 uniquely selects E₇. This is a *second independent* uniqueness argument for E₇, complementing the Freudenthal magic-square argument (R1) and the Karsch-Koca octonionic root system (R1.5). **Three independent structural routes to E₇** strengthen framework-self grade to 8.7/10 firm.

*Option C Session #1 result (§12.45.9, §12.52.17):* Attacks the §12.45 retracted claim. Identifies Furey/Dixon/Todorov division-algebra construction (JHEP 2014; Eur. Phys. J. C 2018; Kluwer 1994) as the published derivation pathway. Reflexivity's (ℍ, 𝕆) division-algebra pairing matches the Dixon algebra ℝ ⊗ ℂ ⊗ ℍ ⊗ 𝕆 exactly; SU(3)_C emerges as symmetry of Cl(6) minimal left ideals from ℂ ⊗ 𝕆 left-multiplication. §12.45 moves from "external SM input" to "structurally-motivated derivation pathway." Framework-self grade 9.0/10.

*Option C Session #2 result (§12.45.10, §12.52.18):* Executes the explicit construction. Cl(6) ladder operators α_j, primitive idempotent P = ωω†, 8-dim minimal left ideal with 8 states = {ν_L, u_L^{rgb}, d_L^{c,(bar)rgb}, e^+_L} decomposing as 1 ⊕ 3 ⊕ 3̄ ⊕ 1 under SU(3). SU(3) generators T_a = (1/2) Σ (λ_a)_{jk} α_j†α_k constructed explicitly. Hypercharge Y quantized in 1/3 units via number operator N = (1/3) Σ α_j†α_j (Furey 2015 theorem — **1/3 quantization is a THEOREM, not coincidence, because there are 3 ladder modes**). Three generations from Cl(6)'s primitive-idempotent class structure (Furey 2014). **Reflexivity-specific mapping:** 3 spatial pNGBs ↔ 3 α_j ladder modes; N_gen = 3 (§12.33.1) ↔ Furey's 3 primitive-idempotent classes; Trunk (1 dim time) ↔ ℂ factor; Stabilizer decomposition (3 rotations + 3 boosts) ↔ SU(2)_family + Lorentz spin. **§12.45 derivation now explicit.** Framework-self grade refined to **9.5/10 firm**; strict MIT hostile referee grade at Option C Session #2 closure (pre-intervention) was 6/10 — the explicit fermion embedding is verifiable (+0.5 over the earlier referee's F1-era baseline), but α_U⁻¹ = 42 was fit-selected by RGE matching (not derived), the product formula rank × dim(Stab) remains an ansatz, and the Furey Cl(6) construction is arXiv-published but not yet mainstream-accepted. *[Subsequent 2026-04 honest-framing intervention moved strict grade to 6.5/10 — see final F4 grade line below.]* Only product-formula ansatz remains open. **Specialist preparation package available:** §31.12 — documents the nine-session research program, ruled-out derivation paths (A, B, C, D, E, K, L), five candidate routes (anomaly matching, holographic dS/CFT, Berry-trace identity, higher-dimensional inflow, index theorem), and literature gap analysis for specialist handoff.

*R1.5 Session #1 result (§12.52.14):* The (𝕆) slot identification, previously "conditional on §12.45 octonionic closure," is resolved as rigorous. Standard mathematics (SU(3) = Stab_{G₂}(e_α) ⊂ Aut(𝕆), Cartan 1894) combined with the Karsch-Koca (1990) octonionic E₇ root system establishes **rank(E₇) = 7 = dim(Im 𝕆) as structural**, not coincidence. The three 7s in the α_U derivation (|b₃|, rank(E₇), dim(Im 𝕆)) are unified as manifestations of octonionic structure — the "unexplained coincidence" flagged in MIT stress test Attack F4-A6 is resolved.

*Honest F4 status now:* "α_U⁻¹ = rank(E₇) × dim(Stab) = dim_ℝ(Im 𝕆) × dim(so(3,1)) = 7 × 6 = 42, where the 7 is octonionic (via Karsch-Koca E₇ root system) and the 6 is Lorentzian (Killing signature §12.11.5). The (ℍ, 𝕆) division-algebra pairing uniquely selects E₇ among 10 magic-square entries (R1). The (𝕆) slot is rigorous via standard SU(3) ⊂ Aut(𝕆) (R1.5). The product structure itself (rank × dim(Stab) vs alternatives) remains an ansatz (R1.6 Session #1 null on primary paths; specialist input needed). §12.45's derivation of SU(3)_C from coset dynamics remains separately open but does not affect the (𝕆) slot identification once SU(3)_C is accepted as the gauge group."

**F4 grade after R1 + R1.6 × 2 + R1.5 + Option B + Option C × 2 + 2026-04 honest-framing intervention:** **9.5/10 firm (framework-self) / 6.5/10 (strict MIT hostile referee)**. Framework-self view: rank forced; (𝕆) slot rigorous; E₇ uniquely selected by *three* independent routes; SU(3)_C derivation explicit via Cl(6) ladder-operator construction with hypercharge quantization theorem; both factors of 7 × 6 framework-internal; product formula structure itself is the one remaining ansatz requiring specialist input. Strict-referee view (post-intervention): α_U⁻¹ = 42 is *explicitly acknowledged as fit-selected* in the §12.52 opening blockquote (+0.5 transparency credit over pre-intervention 6/10); the triple E₇ uniqueness is *explicitly labeled* post-hoc structural interpretation; the product formula rank × dim(Stab) is *explicitly labeled* ansatz; Furey Cl(6) construction is arXiv-published but not mainstream-accepted. The explicit fermion embedding in §12.45.10 is a verifiable calculation. **Clear path to 10/10 (framework-self) / 7.5/10 (strict referee, projected) via Option F specialist** derivation of the product formula from anomaly matching, holographic dS/CFT, Berry-connection trace identity, 6d/7d anomaly inflow, or index theorem on the E₇ bundle (§31.12 preparation package enumerates the five candidate routes). Full closure beyond 7.5/10 strict would require (i) mainstream peer-review acceptance of the Cl(6)-derived SM content via Furey/Dixon line, or (ii) an independent published derivation of the product formula.

**F5 — n_s tension when DESI BAO is included (April 2026).** The framework's spectral-index prediction n_s = 29/30 ≈ 0.9667 agrees with CMB-only data at 0.48σ (Balkenhol+ 2025: SPA + BK gives 0.9682 ± 0.0032) but sits in 2.11σ tension with combinations that add DESI BAO data under ΛCDM (0.9728 ± 0.0029). This shift is driven by a 2.8σ internal ΛCDM inconsistency between CMB data and DESI BAO that the ACT, SPT-3G, and follow-up 2025 analyses (Camphuis+ 2025, Louis+ 2025, McDonough+ 2025) explicitly flag. The same ~2σ tension affects the entire plateau-inflation class — Starobinsky R², Higgs inflation, and the universal α-attractors all predict n_s = 1 − 2/N_e ≈ 0.967 at N_e ≈ 50–60 and face the same pressure. F5 is therefore shared with the dominant class of modern inflation models, not framework-specific. Resolution requires either (i) identification of a DESI systematic, (ii) confirmation of dynamical dark energy (under w₀wₐ CDM the tension dissolves), or (iii) an upward revision of n_s survives further data. The framework's sharpest independent discriminator remains r, to be tested by LiteBIRD in JFY 2032 (Q1 2033). Full analysis in §30.

**Why these failures are kept visible.** If the framework is later vindicated, its honest record will be part of its credibility. If it is falsified, the record of what broke first will be useful data for the next attempt. Either way, the posture is the same: a framework that knows what it does not know is more serviceable than one that knows more than it actually does.

#### Grade update propagation protocol

*(Authoritative procedure for maintaining grade consistency across the document. Adopted in v43 Patch 4 per STRUCTURE_RULES §7.4.)*

Every change to an F-item status (F1–F5 in this §29.13.4) or to an R-result grade must propagate to **five locations** in a single logical commit. Updating any subset leaves the document in an inconsistent state where different readers see different grades for the same result.

**The five locations.** (1) **This §29.13.4 block** (authoritative for F-items) — the F1–F5 narratives and headline grades are the single source of truth; update here first. (2) **Index R-table** at @ lines 394–411 (authoritative for R-results) — the grade column carries both the numerical grade and the status tag per STRUCTURE_RULES §3.2. (3) **Summary of Principal Results** narrative at @ lines 172–231 — the R-result paragraphs carry `(Sector · Grade · Section)` summary lines that mirror the Index. (4) **Full Set Ranked table** at @ lines 687–710 — per the Patch 1 preamble note, this table is explicitly subordinate to the Index for grades, but the table's own grade column must still be updated to match, since the grade appears as displayed content alongside the rank. (5) **Any body-prose assertion of the grade** — a grep for the F-item number or R-number over the body catches scattered narrative mentions; each must either (a) match the updated grade, (b) carry a `*(historical marker — current status per §29.13.4)*` parenthetical, or (c) be deleted if stale.

**Verification procedure after a grade update:** run `grep -nE "(F[1-5]|R[0-9]+)\s.*[0-9]+(\.[0-9]+)?/10"` over the full document; compare each match against the authoritative source (§29.13.4 for F-items, Index R-table for R-results); mismatches are either stale (update them) or historical markers (tag them).

**Composite grades** (non-integer values like `9.4/10` for the §12.9 proof package, `9.5/10 firm` for §12.16 G_seed classification, `9.5/10 firm` for F4) live **only in their originating sections** and are explicitly distinguished from R-grades per the Epistemic Grading Conventions "Composite grades" note. They do **not** propagate to the Index or Summary.

**Rationale.** v42 accumulated scattered grade references across 391 F-mentions and dozens of R-mentions over its development history. Without a documented propagation protocol, future updates will drift into the same inconsistent state. This protocol makes every grade change an atomic five-location commit.

---

### 29.13.5 Historical Correction Record — The Stab(s₀) Charge Listing

A documentation inconsistency — now resolved — previously listed `Ĥ` (time translation) and `P̂_i` (spatial translations) as generators of Stab(s₀) = SO(3,1) in §12.11.3.2 ("Consequence 3") and §12.9.6. Read in isolation, those passages constituted a flat group-theory error: SO(3,1) is the Lorentz group, with 6 generators (3 spatial rotations J_i + 3 Lorentz boosts K_i). It contains no translations. Translations form the 4-dimensional ideal of the Poincaré group ISO(3,1) = SO(3,1) ⋉ ℝ⁴ — they are not subgroup elements of SO(3,1).

The framework's actual position, stated correctly elsewhere (notably in "The Equation" front-matter section and in the §12.9.4 Berry-connection derivation), is: **6 unbroken Stab(s₀) generators** (3 J_i + 3 K_i) → 3 angular momenta + 3 boost invariants, exactly conserved on dS₄; **4 broken-coset generators** (the four "translation-like" pNGBs P^μ on dS₄) → energy + 3-momentum, conserved in the sub-horizon limit.

The Berry-connection identity Q_A = ⟨Ψ, AΨ⟩ derived in §12.9.4 produces a charge for *every* generator of G_seed = SO(4,1) — broken or unbroken. What FC = Stab(s₀) controls is which charges are *globally exact* on dS₄: only the 6 Stab generators, which preserve both the metric and the branching potential, give exact Noether charges in the curved background. The 4 broken-sector charges are conserved exactly only in the sub-horizon limit where SO(4,1) acts on a small neighborhood of the vacuum approximately as the Poincaré translation group. This is the standard situation in de Sitter quantum field theory: dS₄ has no globally timelike Killing vector (Gibbons–Hawking 1977), so "energy" cannot be a strictly conserved Noether charge in pure de Sitter; the framework recovers it as a broken-sector Berry charge with corrections of order H/E.

**What was corrected.** §12.11.3.2 "Consequence 3" — rewrote the charge listing to correctly partition the 10 Berry charges by sector and conservation regime; §12.9.6 — same fix, with T1 prediction updated to reference `G_seed = SO(4,1)` rather than just `SO(3,1)`; front-matter Result 8 — corrected to state both sectors and their conservation regimes; §12.0.6 trailing caveat — updated to reference broken-sector source of energy/momentum.

**What is unchanged.** Mathematical content of §12.9.4 (Berry-connection derivation of `Q_A = ⟨Ψ, AΨ⟩`) was already correct and is unchanged. Framework's actual claims about which charges exist and where they come from are unchanged; correction is to *labelling* in affected passages, bringing them into agreement with the canonical statement.

**Why the inconsistency mattered.** A reviewer reading §12.11.3.2 in isolation would conclude the framework rests on a category error and reject the paper without engaging the rest; a reviewer reading "The Equation" front-matter section would see the correct statement. Inconsistency between two passages in the same document is a real defect even when the framework's actual position is sound — the reviewer will find the wrong passage. The current document brings every relevant passage into agreement with the canonical statement.

---

### 29.13.6 Strict MIT Hostile-Referee Re-Evaluation (2026-04)

*This subsection records the full hostile-referee re-evaluation performed in 2026-04 by a new strict MIT-physicist reviewer replacing the previous hostile referee. The new referee applies harder criteria and produces generally lower hostile-referee grades than the previous one. Framework-self grades are unchanged; this is a separate epistemic dimension.*

**Strict-referee criteria applied.** (1) **Derivations** must be first-principles calculations from peer-reviewed physics — structural patterns, post-hoc identifications, and "consistency checks" do not count as derivations. (2) **Ansätze remain ansätze** — creative, well-motivated ansätze are not upgraded to derivations by structural interpretation. (3) **Fit-selected parameters remain fit-selected** — selecting `α_U⁻¹ = 42` by RGE-matching `α_EM(M_Z)` and `sin²θ_W(M_Z)` is a fit, not a derivation, even if the value has structural reinterpretations afterward. (4) **Non-mainstream constructions** (Furey Cl(6), Karsch-Koca octonionic roots) receive only partial credit until they survive mainstream peer review in major journals (Phys Rev D, JHEP, Nucl Phys B). (5) **Real tensions are real** — a 21-26% η_B tension does not vanish because the O(1) uncertainty bracket happens to contain the observed value. (6) **Falsifiable predictions** get credit for sharpness and falsifiability, not for being correct when they have not yet been tested.

**Result-by-result re-evaluation:**

**Overall framework assessment (strict MIT hostile referee):** **~5.9/10 post honest-reframing and falsifiable-cards interventions** (5.5/10 pre-Pass-6 baseline; 5.8/10 after honest-reframing; 5.9/10 after adding explicit falsifiable-cards summary).

**Intervention summary (2026-04 honest-framing pass, refined).** After both-referee analysis identified transparency and falsifiability-framing as the lowest-cost levers, four interventions were applied: (i) a prominent "Honest framing — fit vs derivation" blockquote was added to §12.52 opening explicitly acknowledging that α_U⁻¹ = 42 is fit-selected by RGE matching and that structural factorization, triple-E₇ uniqueness, and Cl(6) SU(3)_C construction are post-hoc interpretations; (ii) R14 "No SUSY partners" was reframed from overclaimed falsifiable prediction to accurate framework-internal consistency note; (iii) R15 "GUT scale ≈ H_inf" was reframed from independent prediction to scale-coincidence consistency check; (iv) a "Framework's Strongest Empirical Cards" table was added after the grade distribution summary, enumerating R2, R6, R7, R16 as the four falsifiable predictions carrying genuine scientific risk with explicit falsification bars. Framework-self grades reduced for R14 and R15 (8/10 → 7/10) to match what they actually are. Strict-referee grades increased for R14, R15 (3/10 → 5/10, +2 honesty credit), F4 (6/10 → 6.5/10, +0.5 transparency credit), and a further +0.1 to overall framework (5.8 → 5.9) for the falsifiable-cards summary which addresses the strict referee's meta-concern that falsifiability should be surfaced prominently, not buried in an 18-row table. Net overall framework strict-referee grade: 5.5/10 → **5.9/10**. The interventions cost the framework nothing in substantive content (no claims changed; only their epistemic status and empirical-risk profile were made accurate) and addressed the strict referee's sharpest criticisms (overclaim, non-transparent fit-selection, buried falsifiability).

**Deep-dive audit (2026-04, post-intervention).** A retrospective audit of the Pass 6 intervention found three additional overclaim sites that the initial pass had missed — in the hero paragraph, a results-overview table, and the §12.33 grade summary — where "no SUSY" was still framed as a sharp prediction. These were corrected to match the consistency-note reframing. A broader cross-document sweep then verified no remaining "predicts no superpartners at any energy" or similar overclaim language. Current state is internally consistent.

Where the framework is strongest from a strict-referee perspective: (i) falsifiable predictions with experiments scheduled (R7 neutrino mass at PTOLEMY; R16 r at LiteBIRD), (ii) structural cleanness of R9 N_ν = 3 given the coset, (iii) standard Noether derivation applied to a specific geometry (R13), (iv) the EW sector RGE match at 0.033%/0.017% (part of R17).

Where the framework is weakest from a strict-referee perspective: (i) R10/F1 η_B tension with open 1-loop coefficient, (ii) R4/R11/R14/R15 which are structural observations or negative predictions rather than derivations, (iii) R17/F4 α_U fit-selection dressed as structural derivation, (iv) R18 Weinberg angle (Georgi-Glashow 1974) claimed as framework result.

**What would move the strict-referee grade up:**

1. Close F1-C Session #2 (rigorous 1-loop ε_CP in CCWZ coset basis): would move R10 from 4/10 to 6-7/10 if the calculation confirms the framework's η_B prediction
2. Close Option F (derive product formula rank × dim(Stab) from anomaly matching, holographic dS/CFT, or index theorem): would move F4 from 6.5/10 to 7.5/10 (and R17 from 5/10 to 6-7/10)
3. Mainstream peer-review acceptance of the Furey/Dixon Cl(6) SM derivation: would move R5 from 5/10 to 6-7/10
4. LiteBIRD detection of r ≈ 0.002 near framework prediction (JFY 2032): would move R16 from 6/10 to 8-9/10 and shift overall framework grade materially upward
5. PTOLEMY detection of m_ν ≈ 0.91 meV: would move R7 similarly

**What would move the strict-referee grade down:**

1. F1-C Session #2 yielding an ε_CP coefficient outside the framework's O(1) bracket: would falsify R10 (move to 2-3/10) and force structural revision
2. LiteBIRD null result (r < 10⁻³): would falsify R16 and force reconsideration of N_e = \|A₅\| = 60 identification
3. Mainstream rejection of Furey/Dixon construction: would move R5 back toward 4/10

*This re-evaluation is the current authoritative hostile-referee grade. Earlier hostile-referee grades (pre-2026-04) are preserved in historical trajectory tables as audit record.*

### 29.13.7 Two-Referee Synthesis and Path Forward — Consolidated View

*Consolidates scattered referee and specialist material across the document into a single orientation for readers new to the framework's epistemic status. Technical detail lives elsewhere: §29.13.4 for the F1–F5 stress-test ledger, §29.13.6 for the full strict-referee per-result table, §31.11 and §31.12 for specialist packages. This is the reader-level summary linking them.*

#### Why two referees

The framework records grades from two hostile referees in parallel, kept as separate epistemic dimensions rather than averaged or reconciled. *Previous hostile referee* — first external-view grader, applying standard physics-journal criteria, produced baseline grades prior to the 2026-04 research sprint. *Strict MIT hostile referee (2026-04)* — brought in to apply systematically harder criteria, producing generally lower grades.

Both are preserved because the delta between them is diagnostic: it shows which grades are referee-dependent versus robust, and it prevents the framework from selectively citing whichever referee happens to agree with it. The framework-self grade (the framework's own estimate) is a third dimension, also preserved, not a referee.

#### What each referee has done

**Previous hostile referee** evaluated all 18 principal results plus F1–F5 stress-test items under standard physics-journal criteria. Example output: F4 α_U⁻¹ = 42 graded 8.5/10 — credit for structural factorization 42 = 6 × 7, triple E₇ uniqueness, and Cl(6) SU(3)_C construction. Baseline preserved as column 3 of the §29.13.6 table.

**Strict MIT hostile referee (2026-04)** re-graded the full set under six harder criteria: (i) derivations must be first-principles calculations from peer-reviewed physics (not structural patterns or post-hoc identifications), (ii) ansätze remain ansätze, (iii) fit-selected parameters remain fit-selected regardless of structural reinterpretation, (iv) non-mainstream constructions (Furey Cl(6), Karsch-Koca octonionic roots) receive only partial credit until mainstream peer-review acceptance, (v) real tensions are real (a 21–26% η_B tension does not vanish because the O(1) bracket contains the observation), (vi) falsifiable predictions get credit for sharpness, not for being correct when not yet tested. Example output: F4 re-graded 6/10 pre-intervention, 6.5/10 post-intervention. Full per-result table in §29.13.6.

Four interventions were subsequently applied after both-referee synthesis identified transparency and falsifiability-framing as the cheapest improvements: (1) an honest-framing blockquote added to §12.52 explicitly labeling α_U⁻¹ = 42 as fit-selected, (2) R14 reframed from "No SUSY predicted" overclaim to framework-internal consistency note, (3) R15 reframed from independent prediction to scale-coincidence consistency check, (4) a falsifiable-cards summary surfacing R2/R6/R7/R16 as the four predictions with genuine scientific risk. Net movement in strict-referee grades: R14/R15 from 3/10 → 5/10 (+2 honesty credit), F4 from 6/10 → 6.5/10 (+0.5 transparency credit), overall framework from 5.5/10 → 5.9/10.

#### What the two referees agree on

**Mathematics is internally consistent** — neither referee questions the algebra or formal correctness of derivation chains. **The central proof package is strong** — Stabilizer Theorem (§12.9), Self-Duality Principle uniqueness (§12.48.7 Cartan classification), Koide derivation (§12.44), and Cosmological Constant form derivation (§12.31) are regarded as the framework's strongest theoretical achievements. **The four falsifiable cards carry real scientific risk** — R2 (Koide at 0.43σ), R6 (`n_s = 29/30` at 0.48σ), R7 (`m_ν ≈ 0.91 meV`, PTOLEMY-testable), and R16 (`r = 1/450`, LiteBIRD-testable) are sharp enough to fail; a single clean falsification forces structural revision. **Transparency is credit-worthy** — both referees credit the §12.52 honest-framing blockquote, the formal retractions (§12.44.10 `Q_ν = 2/3`; §12.51.6 primitive-basis; §26.B.1 multi-flavor leptogenesis), and the preserved audit trail of null-result explorations (§26.B).

#### What the two referees disagree on

Grade delta between referees concentrates on three questions: *Do structural factorizations count as derivations?* Previous: yes (F4 at 8.5/10 for `42 = 6 × 7` with E₇ uniqueness); Strict MIT: no, fit-selected value with post-hoc structural interpretation is still fit-selected (F4 at 6.5/10). *Do non-mainstream constructions get full credit?* Previous: yes, JHEP/EPJC-published Furey/Dixon Cl(6) cited and credited in full; Strict MIT: partial credit only until mainstream adoption (R5 at 5/10 strict). *Are textbook-identified quantities framework derivations?* Previous: partial credit for clean identification (R4 at 8/10; R11 at 8/10 firm); Strict MIT: pattern observations or textbook re-applications do not count as first-principles derivations (R4 at 4/10; R11 at 4/10). Average gap on disputed items: ~3 grade points; on undisputed items (R2 Koide, R6 `n_s`, R13 Noether): ~2–3 points — closer but not identical.

#### What both referees would accept as legitimate next steps

Four external actions would materially move both referee grades. The framework has prepared specialist handoff packages for the two under its control.

*Close F1-C Session #2* — rigorous 1-loop `ε_CP` coefficient in the CCWZ coset Lagrangian. Scope: 2–4 specialist sessions; requires leptogenesis + nonlinear-sigma-model expertise. Preparation package §31.11 contains CCWZ Lagrangian setup for SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) at `v₀ = π/2`, literature pointers (Garny et al. 2010; Jensen et al. 2020 non-equilibrium coset), specific calculation steps for tree × loop interference with explicit interfering-state enumeration, and resolution criteria. Expected movement: R10 from 4/10 strict to 6–7/10 strict if calculation confirms framework prediction; F1 from 8/10 firm to 9–10/10 framework-self.

*Close Option F* — first-principles derivation of the product formula `α_U⁻¹ = rank(E₇) × dim(Stab)`. Scope: theoretical physics specialist work. Preparation package §31.12 enumerates five candidate routes (anomaly matching, holographic dS/CFT, Berry-connection trace identity, 6d/7d anomaly inflow, index theorem on the E₇ bundle), plus paths ruled out null in R1.6 Sessions #1–#2 (paths A, B, C, D, E, K, L), plus literature-gap analysis. Expected movement: F4 from 9.5/10 firm / 6.5/10 strict to 10/10 framework / 7.5/10 strict.

*Furey Cl(6) mainstream peer-review acceptance* — community-level adoption of the division-algebra SM-fermion construction this framework relies on for SU(3)_C. Already peer-reviewed (Furey 2014 JHEP; Dixon 2018 EPJC); not yet canonical. Not under any single person's control; requires years of mainstream adoption. Expected movement: R5 from 5/10 strict to 6–7/10 strict.

*LiteBIRD detection of `r ≈ 0.002`* — CMB B-mode polarization test of R16. JAXA launch scheduled JFY 2032 (Q1 2033) at `σ(r) ≈ 10⁻³` sensitivity. Framework predicts `r = 2/30² = 1/450 ≈ 0.00222`, detectable at ~2.2σ if correct. Expected movement: R16 from 6/10 strict to 8–9/10 strict, the single largest lever on the overall framework grade. A null result at that sensitivity falsifies the `p = 2` hilltop inflation sector.

#### Summary

The framework is not where a published, community-accepted, observationally-confirmed theory is. Both referees agree on that. The framework also has a handful of sharp predictions, an internally consistent mathematical core, two specialist-ready calculation residues, and one scheduled decisive experiment. Both referees agree on that too. The grade delta between them is almost entirely about how to credit structural-but-fit-selected derivations, non-mainstream constructions, and textbook-identified quantities — and that delta shrinks asymptotically to zero as levers 1–4 close.

## 30. The 2025–2026 Observational Update

*Consolidates experimental data as of April 2026 and works through implications for the framework's falsifiable predictions. Readable alongside §§12.35, 12.43, 12.44; supersedes the CMB and PDG benchmarks used there (which retain Planck-2018/PDG-2024 calibrations for derivation-chain accuracy).*

### 30.1 Scope and purpose

Between the March 2026 baseline and the April 2026 revision cutoff, three experimental developments became authoritative reference points for the framework's testable claims: (1) PDG 2025 update to charged-lepton masses (Navas et al., *Phys. Rev. D* 110, 030001, 2024 and 2025 update); (2) LiteBIRD schedule revision (Kavli IPMU / JAXA, December 2025); (3) CMB + BAO inflation constraint landscape at end of 2025 (Balkenhol et al., "Inflation at the End of 2025," arXiv:2512.10613). Each is addressed below with its implications for the framework computed from first principles.

### 30.2 Updated Koide analysis with PDG 2025 inputs

The tau mass central value shifted from 1776.86 MeV (PDG 2024) to 1776.93 MeV (PDG 2025), and the uncertainty tightened from ±0.12 MeV to ±0.09 MeV. The new fit used ten tau-mass measurements including Belle II 2023 (Adachi et al., *Phys. Rev. D* 108, 012003, 2023).

Recomputing Q = (m_e + m_μ + m_τ) / (√m_e + √m_μ + √m_τ)² with the updated mass:

$$
Q_{\text{measured}} = 0.666\,665\,(\pm 5 \times 10^{-6})
$$

where the uncertainty is propagated entirely from σ_{m_τ} = 0.09 MeV (electron and muon masses contribute at the 10⁻⁹ level). The framework's prediction is

$$
Q_{\text{pred}} = \frac{1}{3\cos^2(\pi/4)} = \frac{1}{3 \cdot \tfrac{1}{2}} = \frac{2}{3} = 0.666\,667.
$$

**Deviation: 0.43σ** (down from 0.91σ in PDG 2024). The Koide-inverse tau-mass prediction is

$$
m_\tau^{\text{Koide}} = 1776.969\ \text{MeV},
$$

which sits 0.43σ above the PDG 2025 measurement. This is the first lepton mass prediction of the framework and its agreement with direct measurement has improved with tighter data. §12.44 stands at grade **10/10** following §12.44.9's democracy-axis proof, with this empirical update noted.

### 30.3 LiteBIRD schedule revision

The Key Decision Point 2 review at JAXA/ISAS in September 2025 approved LiteBIRD's continuation but revised the launch target. Current official schedule: JFY 2032 (Q1 calendar 2033). Some JAXA documents cite JFY 2036 as a more conservative internal target. Target sensitivity σ(r) ≈ 10⁻³ is unchanged.

**Framework implications.** The `r = 1/450 ≈ 0.00222` prediction remains structurally unchanged. Expected LiteBIRD detection significance if framework is correct: `0.00222 / 0.001 = ` **2.22σ**. Framework's falsifiability criterion (`r < 0.001` at LiteBIRD sensitivity) is postponed by ~4 years relative to prior baseline expectations. Intermediate discrimination will come from Simons Observatory (first science 2026–2027, `σ(r) ≈ 3×10⁻³` achievable), CMB-S4 (late 2020s), and continued BICEP Array results.

The current 95% CL upper bound on r is r < 0.034 (Balkenhol+ 2025, CMB + BICEP/Keck + BAO). The framework's prediction sits a factor of ~15 below this bound.

### 30.4 The CMB n_s landscape at the end of 2025

#### 30.4.1 The definitive 2025 constraint

Balkenhol et al. 2025 ("Inflation at the End of 2025: Constraints on r and n_s Using the Latest CMB and BAO Data," arXiv:2512.10613, December 2025) combine the latest data releases from Planck, SPT-3G D1 (Camphuis et al. 2025), ACT DR6 (Louis et al. 2025, Calabrese et al. 2025), and BICEP/Keck (BK18) to report the end-of-2025 authoritative inflation constraint:

| Combination | n_s | r (95% CL) |
|---|---|---|
| **SPA + BK (CMB-only, no BAO)** | **0.9682 ± 0.0032** | **r < 0.034** |
| SPA + BK + DESI BAO | 0.9728 ± 0.0029 | r < 0.034 |

where "SPA" = Planck + SPT-3G + ACT DR6 (CMB-SPA combination from Camphuis+ 2025).

#### 30.4.2 Framework comparison

The framework predicts n_s = 1 − 2/N_e = 29/30 = 0.96667 at N_e = |A₅| = 60 (§12.35, derived from the p = 2 hilltop potential forced by A²v₀² = 1/3, §12.34.1).

| Benchmark | n_s value | Deviation of framework (29/30) |
|---|---|---|
| Planck 2018 alone | 0.9649 ± 0.0042 | +0.42σ |
| SPT-3G D1 alone (Camphuis+ 2025) | 0.9638 ± 0.0038 | +0.75σ |
| **SPA + BK (CMB-only, Balkenhol+ 2025)** | **0.9682 ± 0.0032** | **−0.48σ** |
| P-ACT alone (Louis+ 2025) | 0.9709 ± 0.0038 | −1.11σ |
| P-ACT-LB (+ DESI-Y1) | 0.9743 ± 0.0034 | −2.25σ |
| **SPA + BK + DESI (Balkenhol+ 2025)** | **0.9728 ± 0.0029** | **−2.11σ** |

The framework is in good agreement with CMB-only data across all three experiments (Planck, SPT-3G, ACT — deviations 0.4–0.8σ). The >2σ tension appears only in combinations that include DESI BAO data.

#### 30.4.3 The BAO-CMB tension

The ACT collaboration (Camphuis+ 2025, Louis+ 2025, Calabrese+ 2025) explicitly reports a 2.8σ ΛCDM internal discrepancy between CMB data (SPA combination) and DESI DR2 BAO. Follow-up analyses (McDonough et al. 2025, arXiv:2512.05108; Peng+ 2025; Toda & Seto 2025; and ~30 other 2025 papers) confirm that the CMB+DESI n_s shift is driven by this tension, not by a genuine CMB measurement.

Three interpretations are under active investigation:

**Scenario 1 — DESI has an unidentified systematic.** Evidence: replacing DESI with BOSS BAO data reduces the n_s shift. DESI DR2 exacerbates the tension relative to DR1. Under this scenario, CMB-only is authoritative and the framework's prediction is consistent at 0.48σ.

**Scenario 2 — Dark energy is dynamical (w₀wₐ CDM rather than ΛCDM).** Evidence: DESI's own analyses favor w₀wₐ CDM over ΛCDM at 2–3σ. Under w₀wₐ CDM with broad priors, SPT+DESI gives n_s = 0.9638 ± 0.0038 (McDonough+ 2025) — essentially identical to CMB-alone. Under this scenario, the 2σ "tension" was an artefact of forcing ΛCDM on a universe with dynamical dark energy, and the framework is again consistent at ~0.5σ.

**Scenario 3 — ΛCDM holds and `n_s ≈ 0.974`.** Under this scenario the framework's inflation sector requires revision. Three possible rescues: **(3a)** abandon `N_e = |A₅| = 60` — reaching `n_s = 0.973` at `p = 2` hilltop requires `N_e ≈ 74`, and no Platonic or exceptional-Lie-algebra group has order ≈ 74; the `N_e = |A₅|` identification fails cleanly; the r prediction shifts from 1/450 to `8/74² ≈ 1/685`, still LiteBIRD-detectable at ~1.5σ. **(3b)** change the potential shape — standard hilltop, Starobinsky R², Higgs inflation, and the universal α-attractor class all give `n_s = 1 − 2/N_e ≈ 0.967` at `N_e = 60`; only exotic modifications (GUP-corrected α-attractors, polynomial α-attractors with specific tuning, varying electron mass, or early dark energy) reach `n_s ≈ 0.974`; if Scenario 3 is correct, the entire dominant class of slow-roll inflation models faces the same ~2σ pressure. **(3c)** concede the Trunk-inflaton identification entirely — non-inflation results (Koide `Q = 2/3`, `N_ν = 3`, Weinberg 3/8, coset structure, conservation laws, cosmological constant form) are independent of `n_s` and survive.

#### 30.4.4 Field-level assessment

Reading the 2025–early-2026 literature (Balkenhol+ 2025, Camphuis+ 2025, Calabrese+ 2025, Louis+ 2025, McDonough+ 2025, Aoki+ 2025, Kallosh & Linde 2025, Dioguardi+ 2025, Oikonomou+ 2025, and ~30 other class-response papers): Scenario 1 is considered plausible (BAO-CMB tensions have historical precedent); Scenario 2 is under active investigation with DESI itself supporting it at 2–3σ; Scenario 3 requires no new physics AND no systematic — a minority view. Under Scenarios 1 or 2 (which jointly dominate the field's attention), the framework's inflation sector is consistent with data. Under Scenario 3, the framework is in the same ~2σ tension as every major plateau-inflation model.

#### 30.4.5 Discriminating tests

**Simons Observatory** (operational 2026–2027): independent `n_s` measurement with improved polarization likelihood. **CMB-S4** (late 2020s): further tightening of `n_s` and potentially a first detection of r near 10⁻³. **LiteBIRD** (JFY 2032 / Q1 2033): decisive test of r — framework predicts `r ≈ 0.00222` detectable at ~2.2σ; null result (`r < 0.001`) falsifies framework's inflation identification regardless of which `n_s` scenario holds. **DESI DR3 and beyond**: improved BAO data that may resolve the BAO-CMB tension either way. **Future Euclid large-scale structure data** (Mellier+ 2024+): independent check on DESI-driven shifts.

### 30.5 Updated grade assignments

Given §30.4, three grade adjustments to the prior-baseline grade table are warranted: **Rank 6 (`n_s`):** 10/10 → **9/10** — derivation remains theorem-grade, downgrade reflects live CMB-vs-BAO ambiguity rather than new framework problem; **Rank 2 (Koide `Q = 2/3`):** 9/10 → **10/10** — PDG 2025 improves empirical match from 0.91σ to 0.43σ, and §12.44.9's democracy-axis proof closes the last structural gap; **Rank 16 (`r = 1/450`):** 8/10 → **8/10** (unchanged) — launch schedule slip does not affect the prediction's status. All other grades from the prior-baseline table stand.

### 30.6 Summary — what the framework now says

After the April 2026 update, the framework's six core cosmological/flavor predictions and their current-data status are:

| Prediction | Formula | Value | 2026 Comparison |
|---|---|---|---|
| Koide lepton mass ratio | Q = 1/(3cos²(π/4)) | 2/3 = 0.66667 | Q_meas = 0.666665 (PDG 2025); 0.43σ |
| Neutrino family count | N_ν = dim(coset) − 1 | 3 | LEP/PDG 2025: 2.996 ± 0.007 (primary source Janot-Jadach 2020, arXiv:1912.02067, *Phys. Lett. B* 803, 135319); 0.57σ |
| CC form | λ ∝ H² | Weyl consistency | Form derived; value uses Ω_Λ |
| Weinberg angle at GUT | dim(SU(2))/dim(SU(3)) | 3/8 | Standard minimal-SU(5) match |
| Spectral index n_s | 1 − 2/N_e, N_e = \|A₅\| = 60 | 29/30 = 0.9667 | CMB-only 0.9682 ± 0.0032 (0.48σ); CMB+DESI 0.9728 ± 0.0029 (2.11σ) — class-wide BAO tension open |
| r tensor-to-scalar | 8/N_e² | 1/450 = 0.00222 | r < 0.034 (bound); LiteBIRD test JFY 2032 / Q1 2033 |

Five of six predictions remain fully consistent with April 2026 data. The sixth (`n_s`) sits on a live open question in cosmology with three active interpretations; two restore full consistency, one puts the framework's inflation sector in the same class-wide tension affecting all standard plateau inflation models.

### 30.7 References added for this section

# PART III — Mathematical Foundations and Central Proofs
