## 31.11 Specialist Preparation Package — 1-Loop ε_CP Coefficient (F1-C closure)

#### Rigorous 1-Loop Self-Energy Calculation in CCWZ Coset Lagrangian

**Purpose:** Enable a thermal-QFT / leptogenesis specialist to execute the calculation that would close F1's remaining (S)-rated item (1/(16π)(m/T)² coefficient verification), upgrading F1 from 7.5/10 to 9-10/10.

**Target reader:** Researcher familiar with CCWZ coset construction, thermal field theory (Kadanoff-Baym formalism or closed-time-path / Schwinger-Keldysh), leptogenesis CP asymmetry calculation.

**Estimated effort:** 2-4 sessions of specialist work, or 2-4 weeks of graduate student/postdoc calculation.

---

#### Executive summary of what's needed

The framework's ε_CP formula (§12.25.2):

$$\varepsilon_{CP} = \frac{g_{\rm eff}^4 \sin(2\theta_{CA})}{16\pi (T_{\rm reh}/m_{\rm Trunk})^2} = 7.71 \times 10^{-7}$$

is stated as "the infrared-regulated CP asymmetry from the one-loop self-energy" for a scalar decaying to massless final states at T_reh. Two of three (S)-rated items have been closed structurally (§12.25.13 via F1-C Session #1):
- **Closed.** N_eff = 3/2 derived from N_gen × decay kinematics
- **Closed.** M_j = M_Pl "implicit" recognized as BPY-comparison artifact (thermal regime, not hierarchical)
- **Open.** The specific 1/(16π) × (m/T)² coefficient from rigorous 1-loop calculation

The specific target: **compute ε_CP via explicit 1-loop self-energy calculation in the CCWZ basis for SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) at v₀ = π/2 in the thermal regime T > m_Trunk, and verify whether the coefficient matches 1/(16π) × (m/T)² or differs by an O(1) factor**.

Possible outcomes:
| Result | Impact |
|---|---|
| Coefficient confirmed within 20% | F1 → 9-10/10; η_B prediction sharpens to 30-40% tension |
| Coefficient differs by O(1) | Tension could resolve either direction; framework's η_B quoted value revises |
| Logarithmic enhancement log(m/T) | More substantial framework revision; factor 2-3 shift in η_B |
| Additional sin(2θ) modulation | Framework's max-CP assumption (sin(2θ_CA) = 1) sharpens or requires modification |

---

#### Part I — The CCWZ Lagrangian for SO(4,1)/SO(3,1)

##### Coset parameterization

The coset SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) has:
- **Unbroken H** = SO(3,1) Lorentz, 6 generators: {J^i (3 rotations), K^i (3 boosts)}
- **Broken X** = 4 generators identified as the 4-vector (M^{04}, M^{i4}) where the 5th direction is the dS embedding
- **Goldstones** φ^a, a = 0, 1, 2, 3:
  - φ^0 ≡ Trunk (timelike, radial in dS)
  - φ^i (i = 1,2,3) ≡ spatial pNGBs

##### The vacuum

The framework's Self-Duality Principle (§12.48) derives the unique vacuum:

$$v_0 = \pi/2$$

This is the midpoint of the coset direction (not the origin). The CCWZ Lagrangian must be expanded around this specific value.

##### Coset parameterization and metric

Using a coset representative:

$$\xi(\phi) = \exp\left[i\phi^a X^a / f\right]$$

where f is the decay constant (framework-related to H_inf). At v₀ = π/2:

$$\xi(v_0) = \exp[i\pi X^0 / 2f]$$

The coset metric $G_{ab}(\phi)$ is the Fubini-Study metric on the coset (§12.11 in framework):

$$\mathcal{L}_{\rm kin} = \frac{f^2}{2} G_{ab}(\phi) \partial_\mu \phi^a \partial^\mu \phi^b$$

At v₀ = π/2, the metric components are (framework §12.22):
- $G_{00}^{FS}(v_0) = 9/4$ (Trunk radial)
- $G_{ii}^{FS}(v_0) = \sin^2(v_0) \cdot $ (angular factor) = 1 × (angular factor) at v₀ = π/2

The kinetic term factorizes into Trunk radial mode + spatial pNGB triplet.

##### The potential

The framework's potential is $b_t(\varphi)$ — the branching potential. At the vacuum v₀ = π/2:
- $V(v_0) = \lambda \sim \Lambda$ (cosmological constant)
- $V''(v_0) = (8/3)H^2$ (from §12.34.2)
- After canonical normalization: $m_{\rm Trunk}^2 = (32/27)H^2$ (§12.25.11)

##### Couplings to SM

The framework identifies (§12.33.3):
- Spatial pNGBs P^i ↔ SM leptons (labels, not literal pNGBs)
- Trunk → ℓ + H Yukawa coupling g_eff

The relevant 3-point vertex for Trunk decay:

$$\mathcal{L}_{\rm Yuk} \supset g_{\rm eff}\, \text{Trunk} \cdot \bar\ell_L \cdot H + \text{h.c.}$$

with g_eff = g_GUT/2 = 0.2802 (framework's §12.22.2).

##### What's specific to this framework

1. **Non-compact coset:** SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) has Lorentzian signature (not compact like standard CCWZ applications to SO(5)/SO(4) in composite Higgs). Need to adapt CCWZ formalism for non-compact cases.

2. **Max-CP phase:** sin(2θ_CA) = 1 emerges from v₀ = π/2 via the Berry-connection Stabilizer Theorem (§12.48.3). This is different from generic leptogenesis where sin(2δ) is a free parameter.

3. **Thermal regime:** T_reh/m_Trunk = 12.62 > 1. Standard BPY assumes T ≪ M_1; this is the *opposite* regime.

4. **3 spatial pNGBs interfering:** The broken-coset representation has 3 P^i that could appear in the loop.

---

#### Part II — The 1-loop self-energy calculation

##### Topology to compute

For Trunk → ℓ + H with CP asymmetry, the relevant 1-loop topology is the **self-energy contribution**:

```
       ┌─── H ───┐
Trunk──┤         ├──Trunk  (virtual intermediate state)
       └─── ℓ ───┘
```

with the CP phase entering through the Yukawa coupling structure. At finite T, the propagators are thermal (Bose-Einstein or Fermi-Dirac), and the imaginary part of the self-energy is determined by on-shell cuts in the thermal medium.

##### Key references for thermal self-energy

**Primary reference: Garny, Hohenegger, Kartavtsev, Lindner 2010**
- Paper: "Systematic approach to leptogenesis in nonequilibrium QFT: self-energy contribution to the CP-violating parameter" 
- arXiv: 0911.4122 / Phys. Rev. D 81 (2010) 085027
- Formalism: Schwinger-Keldysh / Kadanoff-Baym
- Key finding: **"medium effects increase the CP-violating parameter"**
- Key finding: **"medium corrections are linear in the particle number densities"** (different from thermal field theory's standard result)

**Coset construction at finite T:**
- Jensen, Liu, Rutter, Sun 2020, "The coset construction for non-equilibrium systems"  
- JHEP 07 (2020) 200
- Formalism: CCWZ on Schwinger-Keldysh contour
- Directly applicable for deriving the framework's thermal CCWZ Lagrangian

**Original thermal leptogenesis:**
- Buchmüller, Plümacher, Yanagida 2005 (BPY)
- Giudice, Notari, Raidal, Riotto, Strumia 2003

##### Specific calculation steps

**Step 1 — Write the CCWZ Lagrangian on the Schwinger-Keldysh contour.**

Following Jensen et al. 2020, extend the framework's CCWZ Lagrangian to the closed-time-path:
$$\mathcal{L}_{\rm SK} = \mathcal{L}[\phi_+] - \mathcal{L}[\phi_-] + \text{IR regulator}$$

with thermal initial conditions at temperature T_reh.

**Step 2 — Identify the loop states.**

Candidate states running in the loop:
- **Spatial pNGBs P^i** — massless at tree level (m² = 0 from shift symmetry + self-consistency λ = Λ/3; MD §12.16.2, §12.30). At finite T they acquire thermal masses ~ gT.
- **SM Higgs** with thermal mass $\sim gT$
- **SM leptons** (relativistic, thermal distribution; Weyl fermions, no tree-level mass in the relevant regime)
- **Trunk itself** in a self-energy topology (the Trunk's canonical pole mass m_Trunk² = (32/27)H² per §12.25.11)

The framework's distinction from BPY: no second "heavy neutrino" exists. The closest mass-scale analogue of a "heavy partner" would be the seesaw RH neutrinos at M_R ≈ 5.25 × 10¹⁶ GeV (§12.49), but these are a different sector from the Trunk.

Candidate interpretation: the thermal IR regulator T_reh is the effective cutoff; the loop sees spatial pNGBs (massless) and SM states (thermal) in the coset+SM coupling.

**Step 3 — Compute Im[Σ(p²=m_Trunk²)] at finite T.**

Using the Garny et al. formalism, the imaginary part from thermal self-energy is:
$$\text{Im}[\Sigma(p)] \propto g_{\rm eff}^4 \int \frac{d^3k}{(2\pi)^3}\, n_B(\omega_k)\, [\text{phase space factor}]\, \sin(2\theta_{CA})$$

where $n_B$ is the thermal distribution. The phase space factor depends on the loop topology and the external momentum p² = m_Trunk².

**Step 4 — Extract the CP asymmetry.**

$$\varepsilon_{CP} = \frac{2\, \text{Im}[\Sigma \cdot \text{tree}^*]}{|\text{tree}|^2}$$

The result should have structure:
$$\varepsilon_{CP} = \frac{g^4 \sin(2\theta_{CA})}{16\pi} \cdot f(m/T)$$

where $f(m/T)$ is the thermal kinematic factor. The framework's quoted form is $f(m/T) = (m/T)^2$; rigorous verification could confirm, modify, or extend this.

**Step 5 — Compare to framework's coefficient.**

Framework's quoted value: $\varepsilon_{CP}^{\rm quoted} = 1/(16\pi) \cdot (m_{\rm Trunk}/T_{\rm reh})^2 \cdot g^4 \cdot 1 = 7.71 \times 10^{-7}$ for framework values.

Specialist output: $\varepsilon_{CP}^{\rm rigorous}$ with explicit coefficient and any additional log(m/T), thermal mass corrections, or multiplicity factors.

---

#### Part III — Specific questions for the specialist

##### Core question

**Q1:** Does the rigorous 1-loop self-energy calculation in the thermal CCWZ basis for SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) at v₀ = π/2 produce the coefficient $\frac{g^4 \sin(2\theta_{CA})}{16\pi}(m/T)^2$, and if not, what is the correct form?

##### Subsidiary questions

**Q2:** Which states run in the self-energy loop?
- Spatial pNGBs P^i (3 of them, **exactly massless at tree level** per framework §12.16.2; thermal masses ~ gT at finite T)?
- SM Higgs at thermal mass $gT$?
- SM leptons at thermal mass?
- Trunk itself via self-energy topology (m_Trunk² = (32/27)H²)?
- Some combination?

**Q3:** Does the Garny et al. 2010 finding that "medium effects increase the CP-violating parameter" apply to this framework? If so, what is the factor of enhancement?

**Q4:** Does the resonant enhancement (maximum-CP regime) predicted by the framework's sin(2θ_CA) = 1 survive in the thermal regime, or is it suppressed by thermal decoherence?

**Q5:** Is the CCWZ coset construction on the Schwinger-Keldysh contour (Jensen et al. 2020) directly applicable to SO(4,1)/SO(3,1), given the non-compact / Lorentzian nature of this coset?

##### Resolution criteria

Calculation closes F1-C to 9-10/10 if:
- Coefficient $1/(16\pi) \cdot (m/T)^2$ verified within 50%
- Any deviations can be absorbed into existing O(1) uncertainties
- The max-CP prediction sin(2θ_CA) = 1 is preserved in thermal regime

Calculation opens a different closure path if:
- Coefficient differs substantially, but reveals a specific structural relationship
- Thermal medium corrections resolve (or worsen) the 30-35% observed tension
- New structural content emerges (e.g., logarithmic enhancement) that provides a sharper prediction

---

##### All numerical values fully specified

| Quantity | Value | Source |

| Coset | SO(4,1)/SO(3,1) | §12.16 |

##### Framework Lagrangian structure (§12.17, §12.38.2)

$$S = \int d^4x \sqrt{-g}\left[\frac{M_{\rm Pl}^2}{2}R + \frac{1}{2}G_{ab}(\varphi)\partial_\mu\varphi^a\partial^\mu\varphi^b + b_t(\varphi) - \lambda(I_{\min} - I(\varphi, s_0))\right]$$

with $I(\varphi, s_0)$ the Fubini-Study distance from $\varphi$ to the reference vacuum $s_0$.

##### Yukawa coupling (§12.33.3)

The Trunk-lepton-Higgs coupling giving rise to ε_CP is:

$$\mathcal{L}_{\rm Yuk} \supset Y_\nu \cdot \text{Trunk} \cdot \bar\ell_L \cdot H$$

with Y_ν² = 128/81 × (framework factors) (§12.42).

## 31.12 Specialist Preparation Package — Product-Formula Derivation (Option F)

#### Derivation of the Product Formula α_U⁻¹ = rank(E₇) × dim(Stab) = 42

**Purpose:** Enable an E₇ / representation-theory / Lie-algebra specialist to attempt derivation of the α_U⁻¹ product formula structure, closing F4 from 9.5/10 to 10/10.

**Target reader:** Researcher familiar with exceptional Lie algebras (E₇, E₈, F₄), anomaly matching, representation theory, or holographic dS/CFT duality.

**Estimated effort:** Uncertain — potentially a major research program. No direct literature precedent identified.

---

#### Executive summary

The framework's most celebrated result — the derivation of the unified gauge coupling $\alpha_U^{-1} = 42$ — has achieved substantial structural closure over 9 research sessions:

- **Factor 7** = rank(E₇) = dim(Im 𝕆) — rigorous via three independent routes (Freudenthal magic-square + Karsch-Koca octonionic roots + Casimir-ratio uniqueness at rank × h^v = 126)
- **Factor 6** = dim(Stab) = dim(so(3,1)) — rigorous from Killing signature
- **Gauge sector content** (SU(3)_C, SU(2)_L, U(1)_Y) — derived via Furey/Dixon Cl(6) construction on (ℍ, 𝕆)

**What remains open:** the *product structure itself*. Why is α_U⁻¹ given by rank × dim(Stab) as a *product*, rather than sum, quotient, or some other combination?

Nine sessions (R1, R1.5, R1.6 × 2, Option B, Option C × 2) have established *that* the formula works (with E₇ uniquely satisfying rank × h^v = 126 by Kostant's formula) and *what* its factors are structurally, but no session has derived *why* the product structure emerges. All attempted derivation paths (A through L, excluding F which is a structural reformulation) returned null.

**The target:** a first-principles derivation of the product formula — most likely via anomaly matching on E₇ Yang-Mills, holographic dS/CFT duality, or a Berry-connection trace identity.

---

#### What nine sessions established (context for specialist)

##### Completed structural work

1. **Freudenthal magic-square** (R1 Session #1, §12.52.12): E₇ = M(ℍ, 𝕆) is forced by Reflexivity's division-algebra pairing; rank(E₇) = 7 is the unique entry giving α_U⁻¹ = 42 under the product formula.

2. **Karsch-Koca octonionic roots** (R1.5 Session #1, §12.52.14): rank(E₇) = 7 = dim(Im 𝕆) is a standard mathematical identity (Koca & Karsch 1990, J. Phys. A 23); the three 7s in the framework (|b_3| = 7, rank(E₇) = 7, dim(Im 𝕆) = 7) unify as manifestations of octonionic structure.

3. **Casimir-ratio uniqueness** (Option B Session #1, §12.52.16): Among all simple Lie algebras, only E₇ satisfies rank × h^v = 126 (where h^v is the dual Coxeter number). This is Kostant's formula dim(g) = rank(g) × (h^v(g) + 1) applied to simply-laced algebras. E₇ is the unique solution.

4. **Cl(6) fermion embedding** (Option C Sessions #1-2, §12.45.9-10): SU(3)_C derived via Furey/Dixon construction on (ℍ, 𝕆). Hypercharge Y quantized in 1/3 units as Furey 2015 theorem. Three generations from 3 primitive idempotent classes matching Reflexivity's 3 spatial pNGBs.

##### Ruled-out paths (from R1.6 × 2 sessions)

The following approaches returned null results:
- Path A: Direct 1-loop β-function matching to rank × dim(Stab) structure
- Path B: Index-theorem on E₇ Yang-Mills bundle
- Path C: CCWZ-level derivation
- Path D: Embedding-indices calculation
- Path E: Root-system trace relations
- Path K: Kac-Moody extension / affine Lie algebra
- Path L: Landau-pole matching

Only Path F survives as a structural reformulation (Casimir-ratio identity h^v(G)/h^v(so(4,1))), not an independent derivation.

---

#### The specific identity to be derived

##### Mathematical target

Derive the relationship:
$$\alpha_U^{-1} = \text{rank}(E_7) \cdot \dim(\mathfrak{so}(3,1)) = 7 \cdot 6 = 42$$

as arising from a specific physical principle, not as a numerical coincidence or ansatz fit to the SM RGE.

##### Equivalent reformulations

Several equivalent forms that any valid derivation must produce:
1. **Product form:** $\alpha_U^{-1} = \text{rank}(G) \cdot \dim(H)$ where G/H = Reflexivity coset, G = E₇, H = SO(3,1) × (E₇/SO(4,1))
2. **Casimir form:** $\alpha_U^{-1} = \dim(E_7) / (h^v(E_7) + 1) \cdot \dim(H) = 133/19 \cdot 6$  
3. **Kostant form (simply-laced only):** $\alpha_U^{-1} \cdot (h^v + 1) = \dim(G) \cdot \dim(H) / \text{rank}$
4. **(dim − rank)/N_gen form:** $\alpha_U^{-1} = (\dim(E_7) - \text{rank}(E_7))/N_{\rm gen} = 126/3 = 42$

Note: Form 4 is independently suggestive — 126 = 2 × dim(root system), and N_gen = 3 is framework-derived. This could be an alternative entry point.

##### Cross-GUT data point

At lower rank / different gauge group, the (dim − rank)/N_gen formula gives:
- E₆: (dim − rank)/N_gen = 72/3 = 24 (matches MSSM unification coupling per MD §12.52.15 table and Option B analysis §12.52.16)
- Standard Model SU(5): not checked in detail

This suggests the formula has some universality beyond E₇, which is either:
- Coincidence (possible at small-integer values)
- A deeper cross-GUT pattern (potentially publishable)

---

#### Candidate derivation routes

##### Route 1: Anomaly matching

**Approach:** 't Hooft anomaly matching on E₇ Yang-Mills with specific matter content might constrain the gauge coupling at the unification scale.

**Relevant prior work:**
- NSVZ β-function derivation via anomaly matching in SUSY gauge theory (Lagrangian with gauge coupling field, current structure S-multiplet)
- Witten 1988 on anomalies and gauge theory vacua
- 't Hooft 1980 consistency conditions

**Specific question:** Is there an anomaly polynomial on E₇ that naturally produces the coefficient rank(E₇) × dim(subgroup) when matched from UV to IR through the Reflexivity coset?

**Literature gap:** Standard anomaly matching derives β-functions and spectra, but not specific dimensionless coupling values like α_U⁻¹ = 42. This is a novel application.

##### Route 2: Holographic dS/CFT

**Approach:** Reflexivity's dS_4 coset structure admits a holographic dual formulation. If the dual theory lives on ∂dS_4 = S^3, the coupling constant of the bulk E₇ Yang-Mills could be determined by the CFT central charge or its analog on the boundary.

**Relevant prior work:**
- Anninos, Hartman, Strominger 2011 on higher-spin dS/CFT
- Maldacena 2003 on dS/CFT correspondence
- Harlow-Stanford 2011 on wave-function interpretation

**Specific question:** In the dS_4 → S^3 holographic dictionary, does the boundary central charge force α_U⁻¹ = 42 on the bulk E₇ gauge field?

**Literature gap:** dS/CFT is not as well-developed as AdS/CFT; the specific application to gauge coupling derivation is largely unexplored.

##### Route 3: Berry-connection trace identity

**Approach:** The framework's Berry-connection formalism (Stabilizer Theorem §12.9) gives $Q_A = \langle\Psi, A\Psi\rangle$ for Stabilizer operators. A trace identity over Stabilizer generators could produce the dim(Stab) factor, while rank(E₇) could emerge from the enveloping algebra's Cartan structure.

**Specific question:** Is there an identity of the form
$$\alpha_U^{-1} = \text{tr}_{E_7}[\text{some operator}] \cdot \text{tr}_{\rm Stab}[\text{some other operator}]$$
that naturally evaluates to 42?

**Literature gap:** No known prior work on Berry-connection traces in gauge-coupling context.

##### Route 4: 6d/7d anomaly inflow

**Approach:** If Reflexivity's 4D framework sits inside a higher-dimensional topological field theory (7D Chern-Simons, 6D (2,0) theory, etc.), the gauge coupling might be determined by anomaly inflow from the higher-dimensional bulk.

**Relevant prior work:**
- Witten 1998 on AdS/CFT and (2,0) theory
- Dabholkar et al. 2020 on holomorphic anomaly and mock modularity

**Specific question:** Does Reflexivity have a natural higher-dimensional uplift (5D or 6D) whose topological invariants produce 42?

##### Route 5: Index theorem on E₇ gauge bundle

**Approach:** Atiyah-Singer index theorem applied to an E₇ gauge bundle on a specific 4-manifold (possibly S^4 or dS_4) could yield an integer invariant equal to 42 times some normalization.

**Specific question:** Is there a natural E₇ bundle whose index or anomaly coefficient is 42?

---

#### Literature gap analysis

**Key finding:** Despite extensive searching (web_search queries on "E7 anomaly matching rank dual Coxeter unification" and related), **no existing literature directly addresses the derivation of $\alpha_U^{-1}$ as rank × dim(subgroup) structures**. This is a genuine research gap.

Standard GUT literature:
- Derives $\alpha_U$ values (~1/40 for MSSM) from phenomenological RGE matching, not from structural arguments
- Treats E₇ unification as a top-down construction, not a mathematically forced outcome
- Does not identify a universal structural formula relating rank and subgroup dimensions to unified coupling

This means any successful derivation of the product formula would likely be:
- A genuinely novel result
- Publishable in a top physics journal as a stand-alone finding
- Potentially generalizable to other exceptional-group GUTs

---

#### What a successful Option F closure would contain

1. **An explicit derivation** of the formula $\alpha_U^{-1} = \text{rank}(G) \cdot \dim(H)$ from a specific physical principle (anomaly, holographic, index, Berry).

2. **Generalization check:** Does the formula apply to other exceptional-group unifications (E₆, E₈)? Check against (dim − rank)/N_gen = 24 for E₆ which matches MSSM.

3. **Identification of the correction structure:** Why does the SM phenomenological α_U⁻¹ ≈ 42.4 (not 42 exactly)? Is the framework's 42 the tree-level value with loop corrections shifting it to 42.4?

4. **Framework impact:** F4 grade moves from 9.5/10 firm to 10/10.

##### Ruled-out derivation paths (documented)

Paths A, B, C, D, E, K, L returned null — specialist should not waste time on these.

##### Framework equations

Master equation: {Q_A, H_S} = 0 (Stabilizer Theorem)
Master action: $S = \int d^4x \sqrt{-g} \mathcal{L}$ with Reflexivity coset + Lagrange-multiplier potential

Relevant formulas for specialist:
$$\alpha_U^{-1} = 42 \quad (\text{phenomenological from SM RGE matching: 42.4})$$
$$\alpha_U^{-1} = 7 \times 6 = \text{rank}(E_7) \cdot \dim(\mathfrak{so}(3,1))$$  
$$\alpha_U^{-1} = (\dim(E_7) - \text{rank}(E_7))/N_{\rm gen} = 126/3$$
$$\dim(G)/(h^v + 1) = \text{rank}(G) \quad \text{(Kostant's formula, simply-laced)}$$

---

#### Expected outcomes

##### Best case
Specialist finds a rigorous derivation path (e.g., anomaly matching with specific matter content, or holographic dS/CFT argument). Framework moves to 10/10 on F4. Paper publishable in top journal as stand-alone result.

##### Likely case
Specialist determines that the product formula is a coincidence (no deep structural reason) and the framework's α_U⁻¹ = 42 is best viewed as a phenomenological ansatz that happens to match rank × dim(Stab). F4 stays at 9.5/10 firm with clear framework-specific uniqueness arguments.

##### Worst case
Specialist identifies a tension: the product formula cannot hold at loop level (renormalization breaks the tree-level structure), requiring framework revision. Would need follow-up work to reconcile.
